      <p>
       The
       <b>
        history of the world
       </b>
       is the
       <b>
        history of humanity
       </b>
       (or
       <b>
        human history
       </b>
       ), as determined from
       <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">
        archaeology
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">
        anthropology
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">
        genetics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">
        linguistics
       </a>
       , and other disciplines; and, for periods since the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_writing" title="History of writing">
        invention of writing
       </a>
       , from
       <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">
        recorded history
       </a>
       and from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secondary_sources" title="Secondary sources">
        secondary sources
       </a>
       and studies.
      </p>
      <p>
       Humanity's written history was preceded by its
       <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">
        prehistory
       </a>
       , beginning with the
       <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">
        Palaeolithic Era
       </a>
       ("Early Stone Age"), followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">
        Neolithic Era
       </a>
       ("New Stone Age"). The Neolithic saw the
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">
        Agricultural Revolution
       </a>
       begin, between 8000 and 5000
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BCE" title="BCE">
        BCE
       </a>
       , in the
       <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">
        Near East
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Fertile_Crescent" title="Fertile Crescent">
        Fertile Crescent
       </a>
       . The Agricultural Revolution marked a fundamental change in history, with humans beginning the systematic
       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">
        husbandry
       </a>
       of plants and animals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETudge199830–31_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETudge199830–31-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As agriculture advanced, most humans transitioned from a
       <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">
        nomadic
       </a>
       to a settled lifestyle as farmers in
       <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">
        permanent settlements
       </a>
       . The relative security and increased productivity provided by farming allowed communities to expand into increasingly larger units, fostered by advances in
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_transport" title="History of transport">
        transportation
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Whether in prehistoric or historic times, people always had to be near reliable sources of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Potable_water" title="Potable water">
        potable water
       </a>
       . Cities developed on
       <a href="/wiki/River" title="River">
        river
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Bank_(geography)" title="Bank (geography)">
        banks
       </a>
       as early as 3000 BCE, when some of the first well-developed settlements arose in
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199913–15_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199913–15-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       on the banks of
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">
        Nile River
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBainesMalek20008_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBainesMalek20008-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBard200064–65_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBard200064–65-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation" title="Indus Valley Civilisation">
        Indus River valley
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChakrabarti200411_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChakrabarti200411-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and along China's rivers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELee200215–42_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee200215–42-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETeeple200614–20_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETeeple200614–20-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As farming developed,
       <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">
        grain agriculture
       </a>
       became more sophisticated and prompted a
       <a href="/wiki/Division_of_labour" title="Division of labour">
        division of labour
       </a>
       to store food between growing seasons. Labour divisions led to the rise of a leisured
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_class" title="Upper class">
        upper class
       </a>
       and the development of
       <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">
        cities
       </a>
       , which provided the
       <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">
        foundation
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">
        civilization
       </a>
       . The growing complexity of human societies necessitated systems of
       <a href="/wiki/Accounting" title="Accounting">
        accounting
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">
        writing
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       With civilizations flourishing,
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">
        ancient history
       </a>
       ("
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">
        Antiquity
       </a>
       ," including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Age" title="Classical Age">
        Classical Age
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013161_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013161-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       up to about 500 CE
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001xii_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001xii-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) saw the rise and fall of empires.
       <a href="/wiki/Post-classical_history" title="Post-classical history">
        Post-classical history
       </a>
       (the "
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       ," c. 500–1500 CE
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001xiv_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001xiv-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) witnessed the rise of
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
        Islamic Golden Age
       </a>
       (c. 750 CE – c. 1258 CE), and the early Italian
       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">
        Renaissance
       </a>
       (from around 1300 CE). The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Modern_Period" title="Early Modern Period">
        Early Modern Period
       </a>
       , sometimes referred to as the "European Age",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013535_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013535-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       from about 1500 to 1800,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       included the
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">
        Age of Enlightenment
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">
        Age of Discovery
       </a>
       . The mid-15th-century invention of modern
       <a href="/wiki/Printing" title="Printing">
        printing
       </a>
       , employing
       <a href="/wiki/Movable_type" title="Movable type">
        movable type
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201263_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201263-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       revolutionized
       <a href="/wiki/Communication" title="Communication">
        communication
       </a>
       and facilitated ever wider dissemination of
       <a href="/wiki/Information" title="Information">
        information
       </a>
       , helping end the Middle Ages and ushering in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">
        Scientific Revolution
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrant200653_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrant200653-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the 18th century, the accumulation of
       <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">
        knowledge
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">
        technology
       </a>
       had reached a
       <a href="/wiki/Critical_mass_(sociodynamics)" title="Critical mass (sociodynamics)">
        critical mass
       </a>
       that brought about the
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
        Industrial Revolution
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013712–14_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013712–14-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and began the
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_history#Late_modern_period" title="Modern history">
        Late Modern Period
       </a>
       , which starts around 1800 and includes the current day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001xix_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001xix-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This scheme of historical
       <a href="/wiki/Periodization" title="Periodization">
        periodization
       </a>
       (dividing history into Antiquity, Post-Classical, Early Modern, and Late Modern periods) was developed for, and applies best to, the history of the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">
        Old World
       </a>
       , particularly Europe and the Mediterranean. Outside this region, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_China" title="Ancient China">
        ancient China
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">
        ancient India
       </a>
       , historical timelines unfolded differently. However, by the 18th century, due to extensive
       <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">
        world trade
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">
        colonization
       </a>
       , the histories of most civilizations had become
       <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">
        substantially intertwined
       </a>
       . In the last quarter-millennium, the rates of growth of
       <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">
        population
       </a>
       , knowledge, technology, communications, commerce, weapons destructiveness, and environmental degradation have greatly accelerated, creating opportunities and perils that now confront the planet's human communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaten20161–13_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaten20161–13-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">
        Prehistory
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">
        Prehistory
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Human_evolution" title="Human evolution">
        Human evolution
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_humans">
        Early humans
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_clock" title="Molecular clock">
        Genetic
       </a>
       measurements indicate that the ape lineage which would lead to
       <i>
        Homo sapiens
       </i>
       diverged from the lineage that would lead to the
       <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">
        bonobo
       </a>
       , the closest living relative of modern humans, around 4.6 to 6.2 million years ago.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChenLi2001444–56_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChenLi2001444–56-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_human" title="Anatomically modern human">
        Anatomically modern humans
       </a>
       arose in Africa about 200,000 years ago,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and reached
       <a href="/wiki/Behavioral_modernity" title="Behavioral modernity">
        behavioural modernity
       </a>
       about 50,000 years ago.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lascaux2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="598" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Lascaux2.jpg/220px-Lascaux2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Lascaux2.jpg/330px-Lascaux2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Lascaux2.jpg/440px-Lascaux2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lascaux2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cave painting,
         <a href="/wiki/Lascaux" title="Lascaux">
          Lascaux, France
         </a>
         , c. 15,000 BCE
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:57px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Venus_von_Willendorf_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2684" data-file-width="1428" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Venus_von_Willendorf_01.jpg/55px-Venus_von_Willendorf_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Venus_von_Willendorf_01.jpg/83px-Venus_von_Willendorf_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Venus_von_Willendorf_01.jpg/110px-Venus_von_Willendorf_01.jpg 2x" width="55"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Venus_von_Willendorf_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         "
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venus_of_Willensdorf" title="Venus of Willensdorf">
          Venus of Willensdorf
         </a>
         ", Austria, c. 26,500 BCE
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Modern humans
       <a href="/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans" title="Recent African origin of modern humans">
        spread
       </a>
       rapidly from Africa into the frost-free zones of Europe and Asia around 60,000 years ago.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stringer2012_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Stringer2012-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The rapid expansion of humankind to North America and Oceania took place at the climax of the
       <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">
        most recent
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_age" title="Ice age">
        ice age
       </a>
       , when temperate regions of today were extremely inhospitable. Yet, humans had colonized nearly all the ice-free parts of the globe by the end of the Ice Age, some 12,000 years ago.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201224–29_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201224–29-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other
       <a href="/wiki/Hominidae" title="Hominidae">
        hominids
       </a>
       such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">
         Homo erectus
        </a>
       </i>
       had been using simple wood and stone tools for
       <a href="/wiki/Millennium" title="Millennium">
        millennia
       </a>
       , but as time progressed, tools became far more refined and complex. Perhaps as early as 1.8 million years ago, but certainly by 500,000 years ago, humans
       <a href="/wiki/Control_of_fire_by_early_humans" title="Control of fire by early humans">
        began using fire
       </a>
       for heat and cooking.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201217_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201217-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They also
       <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_language" title="Origin of language">
        developed language
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">
        Paleolithic
       </a>
       period
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201220–21_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201220–21-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and a conceptual repertoire that included systematic burial of the dead and adornment of the living. Early artistic expression can be found in the form of
       <a href="/wiki/Cave_painting" title="Cave painting">
        cave paintings
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">
        sculptures
       </a>
       made from ivory, stone, and bone, showing a spirituality generally interpreted as
       <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">
        animism
       </a>
       , or even
       <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">
        shamanism
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201232–33_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201232–33-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During this period, all humans lived as
       <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">
        hunter-gatherers
       </a>
       , and were generally
       <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">
        nomadic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201230–31_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201230–31-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Archaeological and genetic data suggest that the source populations of Paleolithic hunter-gatherers survived in sparsely wooded areas and dispersed through areas of high
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_productivity" title="Primary productivity">
        primary productivity
       </a>
       while avoiding dense forest cover.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gavashelishvili23_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gavashelishvili23-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_civilization">
        Rise of civilization
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">
        Neolithic Revolution
       </a>
       , beginning around 10,000 BCE, saw the development of agriculture, which fundamentally changed the human lifestyle. Farming developed around 10,000 BCE in the Middle East, around 7000 BCE in what is now China, about 6000 BCE in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_Valley" title="Indus Valley">
        Indus Valley
       </a>
       and Europe, and about 4000 BCE in the Americas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201236–37_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201236–37-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cultivation of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cereal_crops" title="Cereal crops">
        cereal crops
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Domestication_of_animals" title="Domestication of animals">
        domestication of animals
       </a>
       occurred around 8500 BCE in the Middle East, where wheat and barley were the first crops and
       <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">
        sheep
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goats" title="Goats">
        goats
       </a>
       were domesticated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199911_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199911-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the Indus Valley, crops were cultivated by 6000 BCE, along with domesticated cattle. The Yellow River valley in China cultivated
       <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">
        millet
       </a>
       and other cereal crops by about 7000 BCE, but the Yangtze River valley domesticated
       <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">
        rice
       </a>
       earlier, by at least 8000 BCE. In the Americas,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunflowers" title="Sunflowers">
        sunflowers
       </a>
       were cultivated by about 4000 BCE, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corn" title="Corn">
        corn
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beans" title="Beans">
        beans
       </a>
       were domesticated in Central America by 3500 BCE.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Potatoes" title="Potatoes">
        Potatoes
       </a>
       were first cultivated in the Andes Mountains of South America, where the
       <a href="/wiki/Llama" title="Llama">
        llama
       </a>
       was also domesticated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201236–37_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201236–37-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metal-working" title="Metal-working">
        Metal-working
       </a>
       , starting with
       <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">
        copper
       </a>
       around 6000 BCE, was first used for tools and ornaments.
       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
        Gold
       </a>
       soon followed, with its main use being for ornaments. The need for metal ores stimulated trade, as many of the areas of early human settlement were lacking in ores.
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">
        Bronze
       </a>
       , an alloy of copper and
       <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">
        tin
       </a>
       , is first known from about 2500 BCE, but did not become widely used until much later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201242–43_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201242–43-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sumerian_26th_c_Adab.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="556" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sumerian_26th_c_Adab.jpg/220px-Sumerian_26th_c_Adab.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sumerian_26th_c_Adab.jpg/330px-Sumerian_26th_c_Adab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sumerian_26th_c_Adab.jpg/440px-Sumerian_26th_c_Adab.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sumerian_26th_c_Adab.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform_script" title="Cuneiform script">
          Cuneiform
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">
          writing
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
          Mesopotamia
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Though early "cities" appeared at
       <a href="/wiki/Jericho" title="Jericho">
        Jericho
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catal_Huyuk" title="Catal Huyuk">
        Catal Huyuk
       </a>
       around 6000 BCE,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199913_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199913-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the first civilizations did not emerge until around 3000 BCE in
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201353_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201353-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These cultures gave birth to the invention of the
       <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">
        wheel
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201244_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201244-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">
        mathematics
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201359_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201359-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       bronze-working,
       <a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">
        sailing
       </a>
       boats, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pottery_wheel" title="Pottery wheel">
        pottery wheel
       </a>
       , woven cloth, construction of monumental buildings,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199916_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199916-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">
        writing
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199918_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199918-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Writing developed independently and at different times in five areas of the world:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Egypt (c. 3200 BCE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       India (c. 3200 BCE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201258_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201258-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mesopotamia (c. 3000 BCE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199918–19_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199918–19-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       China (c. 1600 BCE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201260–61_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201260–61-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Mesoamerica (c. 600 BCE).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63_39-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Farming permitted far denser populations, which in time organized into
       <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">
        states
       </a>
       . Agriculture also created food surpluses that could support people not directly engaged in food production.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201334–35_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201334–35-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The development of agriculture permitted the creation of the first
       <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">
        cities
       </a>
       . These were centres of
       <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">
        trade
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">
        manufacturing
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_power" title="Political power">
        political power
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200115_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200115-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cities established a
       <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">
        symbiosis
       </a>
       with their surrounding
       <a href="/wiki/Rural_area" title="Rural area">
        countrysides
       </a>
       , absorbing agricultural products and providing, in return, manufactured goods and varying degrees of military control and protection.
      </p>
      <p>
       The development of cities was synonymous with the rise of
       <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">
        civilization
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [a]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">
        Early civilizations
       </a>
       arose first in Lower Mesopotamia (3000 BCE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200121_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200121-47">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201254–55_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201254–55-48">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">
        Egyptian civilization
       </a>
       along the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nile_River" title="Nile River">
        Nile River
       </a>
       (3000 BCE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBard200064–65_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBard200064–65-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation" title="Indus Valley Civilisation">
        Harappan civilization
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Indus_River" title="Indus River">
        Indus River Valley
       </a>
       (in present-day India and Pakistan; 2500 BCE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChakrabarti200410–13_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChakrabarti200410–13-49">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllchinAllchin1997153–68_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllchinAllchin1997153–68-50">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_China" title="Ancient China">
        Chinese civilization
       </a>
       along the
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">
        Yellow
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yangtze" title="Yangtze">
        Yangtze Rivers
       </a>
       (2200 BCE).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELee200215–42_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee200215–42-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETeeple200614–20_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETeeple200614–20-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These societies developed a number of unifying characteristics, including a central government, a complex economy and social structure, sophisticated language and writing systems, and distinct cultures and religions. Writing facilitated the administration of cities, the expression of ideas, and the preservation of information.
      </p>
      <p>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201343–46_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201343–46-51">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Entities such as the Sun, Moon, Earth, sky, and sea were often deified.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Shrine" title="Shrine">
        Shrines
       </a>
       developed, which evolved into
       <a href="/wiki/Temple" title="Temple">
        temple
       </a>
       establishments, complete with a complex hierarchy of
       <a href="/wiki/Priest" title="Priest">
        priests and priestesses
       </a>
       and other functionaries. Typical of the Neolithic was a tendency to worship
       <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">
        anthropomorphic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Deity" title="Deity">
        deities
       </a>
       . Among the earliest surviving written religious scriptures are the Egyptian
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pyramid_Texts" title="Pyramid Texts">
         Pyramid Texts
        </a>
       </i>
       , the oldest of which date to between 2400 and 2300 BCE.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_history">
        Ancient history
       </span>
      </h2>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cradles_of_civilization">
        Cradles of civilization
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">
        Cradle of civilization
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">
        Bronze Age
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">
        Iron Age
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:167px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2906" data-file-width="4372" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg/165px-All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg/248px-All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg/330px-All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg 2x" width="165"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Giza_pyramid_complex" title="Giza pyramid complex">
          Great Pyramids of Giza
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">
          Egypt
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bronze Age is part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Three-age_system" title="Three-age system">
        three-age system
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">
        Stone Age
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">
        Bronze Age
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">
        Iron Age
       </a>
       ) that for some parts of the world describes effectively the early history of
       <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">
        civilization
       </a>
       . During this era the most fertile areas of the world saw
       <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">
        city-states
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization" title="Cradle of civilization">
        first civilizations
       </a>
       develop. These were concentrated in fertile river valleys: the
       <a href="/wiki/Tigris%E2%80%93Euphrates_river_system" title="Tigris–Euphrates river system">
        Tigris and Euphrates
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">
        Nile
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Indus_River" title="Indus River">
        Indus
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">
        Indian subcontinent
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChakrabarti200410–13_49-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChakrabarti200410–13-49">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Yangtze" title="Yangtze">
        Yangtze
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">
        Yellow Rivers
       </a>
       in China.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">
        Sumer
       </a>
       , located in
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       , is the first known complex civilization, developing the first
       <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">
        city-states
       </a>
       in the 4th millennium BCE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201254–55_48-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201254–55-48">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was in these cities that the earliest known form of writing,
       <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform_script" title="Cuneiform script">
        cuneiform script
       </a>
       , appeared around 3000 BCE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63_39-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201353–54_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201353–54-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cuneiform writing began as a system of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pictography" title="Pictography">
        pictographs
       </a>
       . These pictorial representations eventually became simplified and more abstract.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201353–54_52-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad201353–54-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cuneiform texts were written on
       <a href="/wiki/Clay_tablet" title="Clay tablet">
        clay tablets
       </a>
       , on which
       <a href="/wiki/Symbol" title="Symbol">
        symbols
       </a>
       were drawn with a blunt
       <a href="/wiki/Phragmites" title="Phragmites">
        reed
       </a>
       used as a
       <a href="/wiki/Stylus" title="Stylus">
        stylus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63_39-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201262–63-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Writing made the administration of a large state far easier.
      </p>
      <p>
       Transport was facilitated by waterways—by rivers and seas. The
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       , at the juncture of three continents, fostered the projection of military power and the exchange of goods, ideas, and inventions. This era also saw new land technologies, such as horse-based cavalry and chariots, that allowed armies to move faster.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:187px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Knossos_Bull-Leaping_Fresco.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="591" data-file-width="1000" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Knossos_Bull-Leaping_Fresco.jpg/185px-Knossos_Bull-Leaping_Fresco.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Knossos_Bull-Leaping_Fresco.jpg/278px-Knossos_Bull-Leaping_Fresco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Knossos_Bull-Leaping_Fresco.jpg/370px-Knossos_Bull-Leaping_Fresco.jpg 2x" width="185"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Knossos_Bull-Leaping_Fresco.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Bull-Leaping_Fresco" title="Bull-Leaping Fresco">
          Fresco
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Knossos" title="Knossos">
          Knossos
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Minoan_civilization" title="Minoan civilization">
          Minoan
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">
          Crete
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       These developments led to the rise of territorial states and
       <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">
        empires
       </a>
       . In Mesopotamia there prevailed a pattern of independent warring city-states and of a loose hegemony shifting from one city to another.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In Egypt, by contrast, first there was a dual division into
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_and_Lower_Egypt" title="Upper and Lower Egypt">
        Upper and Lower Egypt
       </a>
       which was shortly followed by unification of all the valley around 3100 BCE, followed by permanent pacification.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBard200057–64_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBard200057–64-53">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Crete the
       <a href="/wiki/Minoan_civilization" title="Minoan civilization">
        Minoan civilization
       </a>
       had entered the Bronze Age by 2700 BCE and is regarded as the first civilization in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201276–77_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis201276–77-54">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Over the next millennia, other river valleys saw monarchical empires rise to power.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In the 25th – 21st centuries BCE, the empires of
       <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">
        Akkad
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-Sumerian_Empire" title="Neo-Sumerian Empire">
        Sumer
       </a>
       arose in
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199936–37_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199936–37-55">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Over the following millennia, civilizations developed across the world.
       <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">
        Trade
       </a>
       increasingly became a source of power as states with access to important resources or controlling important trade routes rose to dominance.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       By 1400 BCE,
       <a href="/wiki/Mycenaean_Greece" title="Mycenaean Greece">
        Mycenaean Greece
       </a>
       began to develop.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPriceThonemann201022_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPriceThonemann201022-56">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In India this era was the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vedic_civilization" title="Vedic civilization">
        Vedic period
       </a>
       , which laid the foundations of
       <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
        Hinduism
       </a>
       and other cultural aspects of early Indian society, and ended in the 6th century BCE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013116–22_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013116–22-57">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From around 550 BCE, many independent kingdoms and republics known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Mahajanapada" title="Mahajanapada">
        Mahajanapadas
       </a>
       were established across the subcontinent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESingh2008260–64_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESingh2008260–64-58">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As complex civilizations arose in the Eastern Hemisphere, the indigenous societies in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       remained relatively simple and fragmented into diverse regional cultures. During the
       <a href="/wiki/Formative_stage" title="Formative stage">
        formative stage
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">
        Mesoamerica
       </a>
       (about 1500 BCE to 500 CE), more complex and centralized civilizations began to develop, mostly in what is now Mexico, Central America, and Peru. They included civilizations such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Olmec" title="Olmec">
        Olmec
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">
        Maya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_civilization" title="Zapotec civilization">
        Zapotec
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moche_culture" title="Moche culture">
        Moche
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Nazca_culture" title="Nazca culture">
        Nazca
       </a>
       . They developed agriculture, growing
       <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">
        maize
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">
        chili peppers
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">
        cocoa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">
        tomatoes
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">
        potatoes
       </a>
       , crops unique to the Americas, and creating distinct cultures and religions. These ancient indigenous societies would be greatly affected, for good and ill, by European contact during the early modern period.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Axial_Age">
        Axial Age
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Axial_Age" title="Axial Age">
        Axial Age
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_philosophy" title="History of philosophy">
        History of philosophy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_religion" title="Timeline of religion">
        Timeline of religion
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_religions" title="History of religions">
        History of religions
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gandhara_Buddha_(tnm).jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2894" data-file-width="1746" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gandhara_Buddha_%28tnm%29.jpeg/170px-Gandhara_Buddha_%28tnm%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gandhara_Buddha_%28tnm%29.jpeg/255px-Gandhara_Buddha_%28tnm%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gandhara_Buddha_%28tnm%29.jpeg/340px-Gandhara_Buddha_%28tnm%29.jpeg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gandhara_Buddha_(tnm).jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddha" title="Buddha">
          Buddha
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Socrates_Louvre.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Socrates_Louvre.jpg/170px-Socrates_Louvre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Socrates_Louvre.jpg/255px-Socrates_Louvre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Socrates_Louvre.jpg/340px-Socrates_Louvre.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Socrates_Louvre.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Socrates" title="Socrates">
          Socrates
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Beginning in the 8th century BCE, the "
       <a href="/wiki/Axial_Age" title="Axial Age">
        Axial Age
       </a>
       " saw the development of a set of transformative philosophical and religious ideas, mostly independently, in many different places.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Chinese
       <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">
        Confucianism
       </a>
       , Indian
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">
        Jainism
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
        Jewish
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">
        monotheism
       </a>
       are all claimed by some scholars to have developed in the 6th century BCE. (
       <a href="/wiki/Karl_Jaspers" title="Karl Jaspers">
        Karl Jaspers
       </a>
       ' Axial-Age theory also includes
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
        Persian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">
        Zoroastrianism
       </a>
       , but other scholars dispute his timeline for Zoroastrianism.) In the 5th century BCE,
       <a href="/wiki/Socrates" title="Socrates">
        Socrates
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">
        Plato
       </a>
       made substantial advances in the development of
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_philosophy" title="Ancient Greek philosophy">
        ancient Greek philosophy
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the East, three schools of thought would dominate Chinese thinking until the modern day. These were
       <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">
        Taoism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Legalism_(Chinese_philosophy)" title="Legalism (Chinese philosophy)">
        Legalism
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">
        Confucianism
       </a>
       . The Confucian tradition, which would become particularly dominant, looked for
       <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">
        political
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">
        morality
       </a>
       not to the force of law but to the power and example of
       <a href="/wiki/Tradition" title="Tradition">
        tradition
       </a>
       . Confucianism would later spread to the
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">
        Korean Peninsula
       </a>
       and toward
       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the West, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
        Greek
       </a>
       philosophical tradition, represented by
       <a href="/wiki/Socrates" title="Socrates">
        Socrates
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">
        Plato
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">
        Aristotle
       </a>
       , and other philosophers,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200163_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200163-59">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       along with accumulated science, technology, and culture, diffused throughout
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       , Egypt, the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">
        Middle East
       </a>
       , and Northwest India, starting in the 4th century BCE after the conquests of Alexander III of
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Macedonians" title="Ancient Macedonians">
        Macedon
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">
        Alexander the Great
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200170–71_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200170–71-60">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_empires">
        Regional empires
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">
        Civilization
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">
        Empire
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The millennium from 500 BCE to 500 CE saw a series of empires of unprecedented size develop. Well-trained professional armies, unifying ideologies, and advanced bureaucracies created the possibility for emperors to rule over large domains whose populations could attain numbers upwards of tens of millions of subjects. The great
       <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">
        empires
       </a>
       depended on
       <a href="/wiki/Military" title="Military">
        military
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">
        annexation
       </a>
       of territory and on the formation of defended settlements to become agricultural centres. The relative peace that the empires brought encouraged
       <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">
        international trade
       </a>
       , most notably the massive trade routes in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       , the maritime trade web in the Indian Ocean, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">
        Silk Road
       </a>
       . In southern Europe, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
        Greeks
       </a>
       (and later the
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
        Romans
       </a>
       ), in an era known as "
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">
        classical antiquity
       </a>
       ," established cultures whose practices, laws, and customs are considered the foundation of contemporary
       <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">
        Western culture
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Persepolis_The_Persian_Soldiers.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1284" data-file-width="1908" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Persepolis_The_Persian_Soldiers.jpg/220px-Persepolis_The_Persian_Soldiers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Persepolis_The_Persian_Soldiers.jpg/330px-Persepolis_The_Persian_Soldiers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Persepolis_The_Persian_Soldiers.jpg/440px-Persepolis_The_Persian_Soldiers.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Persepolis_The_Persian_Soldiers.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Persepolis" title="Persepolis">
          Persepolis
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
          Achaemenid Empire
         </a>
         , 5th century BCE
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Parthenon_in_Athens.jpg">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Parthenon_in_Athens.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Parthenon" title="Parthenon">
          Parthenon
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athenian_Empire" title="Athenian Empire">
          Athenian Empire
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ashoka_pillar_at_Vaishali,_Bihar,_India.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Ashoka_pillar_at_Vaishali%2C_Bihar%2C_India.jpg/220px-Ashoka_pillar_at_Vaishali%2C_Bihar%2C_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Ashoka_pillar_at_Vaishali%2C_Bihar%2C_India.jpg/330px-Ashoka_pillar_at_Vaishali%2C_Bihar%2C_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Ashoka_pillar_at_Vaishali%2C_Bihar%2C_India.jpg/440px-Ashoka_pillar_at_Vaishali%2C_Bihar%2C_India.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ashoka_pillar_at_Vaishali,_Bihar,_India.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashoka_pillar" title="Ashoka pillar">
          Pillar
         </a>
         erected by
         <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
          India
         </a>
         's
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maurya_Dynasty" title="Maurya Dynasty">
          Maurya Dynasty
         </a>
         Emperor
         <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">
          Ashoka
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roma-colonna_di_trainao.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Roma-colonna_di_trainao.jpg/220px-Roma-colonna_di_trainao.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Roma-colonna_di_trainao.jpg/330px-Roma-colonna_di_trainao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Roma-colonna_di_trainao.jpg/440px-Roma-colonna_di_trainao.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roma-colonna_di_trainao.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Trajan%27s_Column" title="Trajan's Column">
          Trajan's Column
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">
          Rome
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="576" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n.jpg/220px-Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n.jpg/330px-Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n.jpg/440px-Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terrakottaarm%C3%A9n.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Terracotta_Army" title="Terracotta Army">
          Terracotta army
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
          China
         </a>
         , c. 210 BCE
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stela_aksum.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="511" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Stela_aksum.jpg/220px-Stela_aksum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Stela_aksum.jpg/330px-Stela_aksum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Stela_aksum.jpg/440px-Stela_aksum.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stela_aksum.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obelisk_of_Aksum" title="Obelisk of Aksum">
          Obelisk of Aksum
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
          Ethiopia
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There were a number of regional empires during this period. The kingdom of the
       <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">
        Medes
       </a>
       helped to destroy the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assyrian_Empire" title="Assyrian Empire">
        Assyrian Empire
       </a>
       in tandem with the nomadic
       <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
        Scythians
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Babylonians" title="Babylonians">
        Babylonians
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">
        Nineveh
       </a>
       , the capital of Assyria, was sacked by the Medes in 612 BCE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013110_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013110-61">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_Empire" title="Median Empire">
        Median Empire
       </a>
       gave way to successive
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran" title="History of Iran">
        Iranian
       </a>
       empires, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Achaemenid Empire
       </a>
       (550–330 BCE) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">
        Sasanian Empire
       </a>
       (224–651 CE).
      </p>
      <p>
       Several empires began in modern-day Greece. First was the
       <a href="/wiki/Delian_League" title="Delian League">
        Delian League
       </a>
       (from 477 BCE)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin2000106–07_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin2000106–07-62">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the succeeding
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athenian_Empire" title="Athenian Empire">
        Athenian Empire
       </a>
       (454–404 BCE), centred in present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       . Later,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">
        Alexander the Great
       </a>
       (356–323 BCE), of
       <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">
        Macedon
       </a>
       , founded an empire of conquest, extending from present-day Greece to present-day India.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGolden201125_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGolden201125-63">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The empire divided shortly after his death, but the influence of his
       <a href="/wiki/Hellenization" title="Hellenization">
        Hellenistic
       </a>
       successors made for an extended
       <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">
        Hellenistic period
       </a>
       (323–31 BCE)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       throughout the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       In Asia, the
       <a href="/wiki/Maurya_Empire" title="Maurya Empire">
        Maurya Empire
       </a>
       (322–185 BCE) existed in present-day
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">
        India
       </a>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the 3rd century BCE, most of
       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">
        South Asia
       </a>
       was united to the Maurya Empire by
       <a href="/wiki/Chandragupta_Maurya" title="Chandragupta Maurya">
        Chandragupta Maurya
       </a>
       and flourished under
       <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">
        Ashoka the Great
       </a>
       . From the 3rd century CE, the
       <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">
        Gupta dynasty
       </a>
       oversaw the period referred to as ancient India's Golden Age. From the 4th to 6th centuries, northern India was ruled by the
       <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">
        Gupta Empire
       </a>
       . In southern India, three prominent
       <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_people" title="Dravidian people">
        Dravidian
       </a>
       kingdoms emerged: the
       <a href="/wiki/Chera_dynasty" title="Chera dynasty">
        Cheras
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">
        Cholas
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pandyan_dynasty" title="Pandyan dynasty">
        Pandyas
       </a>
       . The ensuing stability contributed to heralding in the golden age of
       <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">
        Hindu
       </a>
       culture in the 4th and 5th centuries.
      </p>
      <p>
       In Europe, the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="History of the Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , centred in present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       , began in the 7th century BCE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis2012106–07_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis2012106–07-68">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Beginning in the 3rd century BCE, the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Roman Republic
       </a>
       began expanding its territory through conquest and alliances.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly20074–6_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly20074–6-69">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the time of
       <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">
        Augustus
       </a>
       (63 BCE – 14 CE), who became the first Roman Emperor, Rome had already established dominion over most of the Mediterranean. The empire would continue to grow, controlling much of the land from
       <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">
        England
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">
        Mesopotamia
       </a>
       , reaching its greatest extent under the emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">
        Trajan
       </a>
       (d. 117 CE). In the 3rd century CE, the empire would split into western and eastern regions, with (usually) separate emperors. The Western empire would
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">
        fall
       </a>
       , in 476 CE, to German influence under
       <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">
        Odoacer
       </a>
       . The eastern empire, now known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       , with its capital at
       <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">
        Constantinople
       </a>
       , would continue for another thousand years, until overthrown by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       in 1453 CE.
      </p>
      <p>
       In China, the
       <a href="/wiki/Qin_dynasty" title="Qin dynasty">
        Qin dynasty
       </a>
       (221–206 BCE), the first imperial dynasty of China, was followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">
        Han Empire
       </a>
       (206 BCE – 220 CE). The Han Dynasty was comparable in power and influence to the Roman Empire that lay at the other end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">
        Silk Road
       </a>
       . Han China developed advanced cartography, shipbuilding, and navigation. The Chinese invented
       <a href="/wiki/Blast_furnace" title="Blast furnace">
        blast furnaces
       </a>
       , and created finely tuned copper instruments. As with other empires during the Classical Period, Han China advanced significantly in the areas of government, education, mathematics, astronomy, technology, and many others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1_Mayan_observatory.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="853" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1_Mayan_observatory.jpg/220px-Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1_Mayan_observatory.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1_Mayan_observatory.jpg/330px-Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1_Mayan_observatory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1_Mayan_observatory.jpg/440px-Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1_Mayan_observatory.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chich%C3%A9n_Itz%C3%A1_Mayan_observatory.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">
          Maya
         </a>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronomical_observatory" title="Astronomical observatory">
          observatory
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Chichen_Itza" title="Chichen Itza">
          Chichen Itza
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
          Mexico
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In Africa, the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">
        Kingdom of Aksum
       </a>
       , centred in present-day Ethiopia, established itself by the 1st century CE as a major trading empire, dominating its neighbours in South
       <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">
        Arabia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kush" title="Kingdom of Kush">
        Kush
       </a>
       and controlling the
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">
        Red Sea
       </a>
       trade. It minted its own currency and carved enormous monolithic
       <a href="/wiki/Stele" title="Stele">
        steles
       </a>
       such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Obelisk_of_Axum" title="Obelisk of Axum">
        Obelisk of Axum
       </a>
       to mark their emperors' graves.
      </p>
      <p>
       Successful regional empires were also established in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       , arising from cultures established as early as 2500 BCE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFagan2005390,_396_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFagan2005390,_396-71">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Mesoamerica" title="History of Mesoamerica">
        Mesoamerica
       </a>
       , vast pre-Columbian societies were built, the most notable being the
       <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_civilization" title="Zapotec civilization">
        Zapotec Empire
       </a>
       (700 BCE – 1521 CE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">
        Maya civilization
       </a>
       , which reached its highest state of development during the Mesoamerican Classic period (c. 250–900 CE),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoe201191_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoe201191-73">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but continued throughout the Post-Classic period until the arrival of the Spanish in the 16th century CE. Maya civilization arose as the
       <a href="/wiki/Olmec" title="Olmec">
        Olmec
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Mother_culture" title="Mother culture">
        mother culture
       </a>
       gradually declined. The great Mayan
       <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">
        city-states
       </a>
       slowly rose in number and prominence, and Maya culture spread throughout the
       <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">
        Yucatán
       </a>
       and surrounding areas. The later empire of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">
        Aztecs
       </a>
       was built on neighbouring cultures and was influenced by conquered peoples such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Toltec" title="Toltec">
        Toltecs
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Some areas experienced slow but steady technological advances, with important developments such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Stirrup" title="Stirrup">
        stirrup
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moldboard_plow" title="Moldboard plow">
        moldboard plough
       </a>
       arriving every few centuries. There were, however, in some regions, periods of rapid technological progress. Most important, perhaps, was the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       area during the
       <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">
        Hellenistic period
       </a>
       , when hundreds of technologies were invented.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Such periods were followed by periods of technological decay, as during the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       's decline and
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">
        fall
       </a>
       and the ensuing
       <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">
        early medieval
       </a>
       period.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Declines.2C_falls_and_resurgence">
       </span>
