       <span class="mw-headline" id="Declines,_falls_and_resurgence">
        Declines, falls and resurgence
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The empires faced common problems associated with maintaining huge armies and supporting a central bureaucracy. These costs fell most heavily on the
       <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">
        peasantry
       </a>
       , while land-owning
       <a href="/wiki/Magnate" title="Magnate">
        magnates
       </a>
       increasingly evaded centralized control and its costs.
       <a href="/wiki/Barbarian" title="Barbarian">
        Barbarian
       </a>
       pressure on the frontiers hastened internal dissolution.
       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
        China
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Han_dynasty" title="Han dynasty">
        Han dynasty
       </a>
       fell into
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_war" title="Civil war">
        civil war
       </a>
       in 220 CE, beginning the
       <a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms" title="Three Kingdoms">
        Three Kingdoms
       </a>
       period, while its
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman
       </a>
       counterpart became increasingly decentralized and divided about the same time in what is known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Crisis_of_the_Third_Century" title="Crisis of the Third Century">
        Crisis of the Third Century
       </a>
       . The great empires of Eurasia were all located on temperate and subtropical coastal plains. From the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">
        Central Asian
       </a>
       steppes, horse-based nomads (mainly Mongols and Turks) dominated a large part of the continent. The development of the
       <a href="/wiki/Stirrup" title="Stirrup">
        stirrup
       </a>
       and the breeding of horses strong enough to carry a fully armed archer made the nomads a constant threat to the more settled civilizations.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pantheon_Rome_04_2016_6460.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Pantheon_Rome_04_2016_6460.jpg/140px-Pantheon_Rome_04_2016_6460.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Pantheon_Rome_04_2016_6460.jpg/210px-Pantheon_Rome_04_2016_6460.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Pantheon_Rome_04_2016_6460.jpg/280px-Pantheon_Rome_04_2016_6460.jpg 2x" width="140"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pantheon_Rome_04_2016_6460.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Pantheon,_Rome" title="Pantheon, Rome">
          Pantheon, Rome
         </a>
         , now a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
          Catholic church
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The gradual break-up of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , spanning several centuries after the 2nd century CE, coincided with the spread of
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       outward from the Middle East.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200195,_99_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200195,_99-75">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Western Roman Empire fell under the domination of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_tribes" title="Germanic tribes">
        Germanic tribes
       </a>
       in the 5th century,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins199980–99_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins199980–99-76">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and these
       <a href="/wiki/Polity" title="Polity">
        polities
       </a>
       gradually developed into a number of warring states, all associated in one way or another with the
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Catholic Church
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1999100–15_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1999100–15-77">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The remaining part of the Roman Empire, in the eastern Mediterranean, continued as what came to be called the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200197,_103_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200197,_103-78">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Centuries later, a limited unity would be restored to western Europe through the establishment in 962 of a revived "Roman Empire",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1999404_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1999404-79">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       later called the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoyn1991122–23_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoyn1991122–23-80">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       comprising a number of states in what is now Germany, Austria, Switzerland, Czech Republic, Belgium, Italy, and parts of France.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnson199623_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnson199623-82">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In China,
       <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">
        dynasties
       </a>
       would rise and fall, but, by sharp contrast to the Mediterranean-European world, dynastic unity would be restored. After the fall of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Han_Dynasty" title="Eastern Han Dynasty">
        Eastern Han Dynasty
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the demise of the Three Kingdoms,
       <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">
        nomadic
       </a>
       tribes from the north began to invade in the 4th century, eventually conquering areas of northern China and setting up many small kingdoms.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sui_Dynasty" title="Sui Dynasty">
        Sui Dynasty
       </a>
       successfully reunified the whole of China
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGascoigne200390–92_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGascoigne200390–92-84">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in 581,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGernet1996237–38_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGernet1996237–38-85">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and laid the foundations for a Chinese golden age under the
       <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">
        Tang dynasty
       </a>
       (618–907).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-classical_history">
        Post-classical history
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Post-classical_history" title="Post-classical history">
        Post-classical history
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG/220px-Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG/330px-Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG/440px-Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Timbuktu" title="University of Timbuktu">
          University of Timbuktu
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">
          Mali
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Post-classical Era, though deriving its name from the Eurocentric era of "
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">
        Classical antiquity
       </a>
       ", refers to a broader geographic sweep. The era is commonly dated from the 5th-century
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">
        fall of the Western Roman Empire
       </a>
       , which fragmented into many separate kingdoms, some of which would later be confederated under the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       . The Eastern Roman, or
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine, Empire
       </a>
       survived until late in the Post-classical, or Medieval, period. The Post-classical period also encompasses the
       <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">
        Early Muslim conquests
       </a>
       , the subsequent
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
        Islamic Golden Age
       </a>
       , and the commencement and expansion of the
       <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">
        Arab slave trade
       </a>
       , followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">
        Mongol invasions
       </a>
       in the Middle East and Central Asia,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and the founding around 1280 of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShaw197613_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw197613-86">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">
        South Asia
       </a>
       saw a series of
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_kingdoms_of_India" title="Middle kingdoms of India">
        middle kingdoms of India
       </a>
       , followed by the establishment of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_empires_in_India" title="Islamic empires in India">
        Islamic empires in India
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In western Africa, the
       <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">
        Mali Empire
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">
        Songhai Empire
       </a>
       developed. On the southeast coast of Africa, Arabic ports were established where
       <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
        gold
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">
        spices
       </a>
       , and other commodities were traded. This allowed Africa to join the
       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">
        Southeast Asia
       </a>
       trading system, bringing it contact with Asia; this, along with Muslim culture, resulted in the
       <a href="/wiki/Swahili_culture" title="Swahili culture">
        Swahili culture
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-Imperial_China" title="Mid-Imperial China">
        Chinese Empire
       </a>
       experienced the successive
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sui_Dynasty" title="Sui Dynasty">
        Sui
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">
        Tang
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">
        Song
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">
        Yuan
       </a>
       , early
       <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">
        Ming
       </a>
       Dynasties. Middle Eastern trade routes along the Indian Ocean, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">
        Silk Road
       </a>
       through the Gobi Desert, provided limited economic and cultural contact between Asian and European civilizations. During the same period, civilizations in the Americas, such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inca" title="Inca">
        Inca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">
        Maya
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">
        Aztec
       </a>
       , reached their height; all would be seriously compromised by contact with
       <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">
        European colonists
       </a>
       at the beginning of the
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">
        Modern period
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Middle_East.2C_Central_Asia_and_North_Africa">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East,_Central_Asia_and_North_Africa">
        Middle East, Central Asia and North Africa
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Middle_East" title="History of the Middle East">
        History of the Middle East
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Central_Asia" title="History of Central Asia">
        History of Central Asia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_Africa" title="History of North Africa">
        History of North Africa
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
        Islamic Golden Age
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Prior to the advent of Islam in the 7th century, the Middle East was dominated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       and the Persian
       <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">
        Sasanian Empire
       </a>
       , which constantly fought each other for control of several disputed regions. This was also a cultural battle, with the Byzantine Hellenistic and Christian culture competing against the Persian Iranian traditions and
       <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">
        Zoroastrian religion
       </a>
       . The formation of the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Islam" title="History of Islam">
        Islamic religion
       </a>
       created a new contender that quickly surpassed both of these empires. Islam greatly affected the
       <a href="/wiki/Political_history" title="Political history">
        political
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_history" title="Economic history">
        economic
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">
        military history
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">
        Old World
       </a>
       , especially the Middle East.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan,_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3551" data-file-width="4620" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg/220px-Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg/330px-Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg/440px-Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan,_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Kairouan" title="Great Mosque of Kairouan">
          Great Mosque of Kairouan
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
          Tunisia
         </a>
         , founded 670 CE
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       From their centre on the Arabian Peninsula, Muslims began their expansion during the early Postclassical Era. By 750 CE, they came to conquer most of the Near East, North Africa, and parts of Europe, ushering in an era of learning, science, and invention known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
        Islamic Golden Age
       </a>
       . The knowledge and skills of the ancient Near East, Greece, and Persia were preserved in the Postclassical Era by Muslims, who also added new and important innovations from outside, such as the manufacture of paper from China and decimal positional numbering from India.
      </p>
      <p>
       Much of this learning and development can be linked to geography. Even prior to Islam's presence, the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">
        Mecca
       </a>
       had served as a centre of trade in Arabia, and the Islamic prophet
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
        Muhammad
       </a>
       himself was a merchant. With the new Islamic tradition of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">
         Hajj
        </a>
       </i>
       , the pilgrimage to Mecca, the city became even more a centre for exchanging goods and ideas. The influence held by Muslim merchants over African-Arabian and Arabian-Asian trade routes was tremendous. As a result, Islamic civilization grew and expanded on the basis of its merchant economy, in contrast to the Europeans, Indians, and Chinese, who based their societies on an agricultural landholding nobility. Merchants brought goods and their Islamic faith to
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">
        China
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_conquests_on_the_Indian_subcontinent" title="Muslim conquests on the Indian subcontinent">
        India
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Islam in Southeast Asia">
        southeast Asia
       </a>
       , and the kingdoms of western
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Africa" title="Islam in Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       , and returned with new discoveries and inventions.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1566" data-file-width="4015" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg/250px-Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg/375px-Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg/500px-Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">
          Crusader
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Krak_des_Chevaliers" title="Krak des Chevaliers">
          Krak des Chevaliers
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
          Syria
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Motivated by religion and dreams of conquest, European kings launched a number of
       <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">
        Crusades
       </a>
       to try to roll back Muslim power and retake the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">
        Holy Land
       </a>
       . The Crusades were ultimately unsuccessful and served more to weaken the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Empire
       </a>
       especially with the 1204
       <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Constantinople_(1204)" title="Sack of Constantinople (1204)">
        sack of Constantinople
       </a>
       , which began to lose increasing amounts of territory to the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Turks
       </a>
       . Arab domination of the region ended in the mid-11th century with the arrival of the
       <a href="/wiki/Seljuq_dynasty" title="Seljuq dynasty">
        Seljuq Turks
       </a>
       , migrating south from the Turkic homelands in Central Asia. In the early 13th century, a new wave of invaders, the
       <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">
        Mongol Empire
       </a>
       's armies, swept through the region but were eventually eclipsed by the Turks
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and the founding of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       in modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       around 1280.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShaw197613_86-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw197613-86">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Starting with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sui_Dynasty" title="Sui Dynasty">
        Sui Dynasty
       </a>
       (581–618), the Chinese began expanding into eastern
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">
        Central Asia
       </a>
       , and had to deal with
       <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">
        Turkic
       </a>
       nomads, who were becoming the most dominant ethnic group in Central Asia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEbreyWalthallPalais2006113_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEbreyWalthallPalais2006113-87">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEXue1992149–52,_257–64_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEXue1992149–52,_257–64-88">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Originally the relationship was largely cooperative, but in 630 the
       <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">
        Tang dynasty
       </a>
       began an offensive against the Turks,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEXue1992226–27_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEXue1992226–27-89">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       capturing areas of the Mongolian Ordos Desert. The Tang Empire competed with the
       <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Empire" title="Tibetan Empire">
        Tibetan Empire
       </a>
       for control of areas in Inner and Central Asia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhitfield2004193_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhitfield2004193-90">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 8th century, Islam began to penetrate the region and soon became the sole faith of most of the population, though Buddhism remained strong in the east.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The desert nomads of
       <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">
        Arabia
       </a>
       could militarily match the nomads of the steppe, and the early
       <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">
        Arab Empire
       </a>
       gained control over parts of Central Asia.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Hephthalite_Empire" title="Hephthalite Empire">
        Hephthalites
       </a>
       were the most powerful of the nomad groups in the 6th and 7th centuries, and controlled much of the region. In the 9th through 13th centuries the region was divided among several powerful states, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Samanid_Empire" title="Samanid Empire">
        Samanid dynasty
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Seljuq_dynasty" title="Seljuq dynasty">
        Seljuq dynasty
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_dynasty" title="Khwarazmian dynasty">
        Khwarezmid Empire
       </a>
       . The most spectacular power to rise out of Central Asia developed when
       <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">
        Genghis Khan
       </a>
       united the tribes of Mongolia. The
       <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">
        Mongol Empire
       </a>
       spread to comprise all of Central Asia and China as well as large parts of Russia, and the Middle East.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       After Genghis Khan died in 1227,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001153_92-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001153-92">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       most of Central Asia continued to be dominated by the successor
       <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">
        Chagatai Khanate
       </a>
       . In 1369,
       <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">
        Timur
       </a>
       , a Turkic leader in the Mongol military tradition, conquered most of the region and founded the
       <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">
        Timurid Empire
       </a>
       . Timur's large empire collapsed soon after his death, however. The region then became divided into a series of smaller khanates that were created by the
       <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">
        Uzbeks
       </a>
       . These included the
       <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Khiva" title="Khanate of Khiva">
        Khanate of Khiva
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Bukhara" title="Khanate of Bukhara">
        Khanate of Bukhara
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kokand" title="Khanate of Kokand">
        Khanate of Kokand
       </a>
       , all of whose capitals are located in present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">
        Uzbekistan
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       saw the rise of polities formed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">
        Berbers
       </a>
       , such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Marinid_dynasty" title="Marinid dynasty">
        Marinid dynasty
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Morocco
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Zayyanid_dynasty" title="Zayyanid dynasty">
        Zayyanid dynasty
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Hafsid_dynasty" title="Hafsid dynasty">
        Hafsid dynasty
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
        Tunisia
       </a>
       . The region will later be called the
       <a href="/wiki/Barbary_Coast" title="Barbary Coast">
        Barbary Coast
       </a>
       and will host pirates and privateers who will use several North African ports for their raids against the coastal towns of several European countries in search of slaves to be sold in North African markets as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Barbary_slave_trade" title="Barbary slave trade">
        Barbary slave trade
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">
        Europe
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Europe" title="History of Europe">
        History of Europe
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Europe during the
       <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">
        Early Middle Ages
       </a>
       was characterized by depopulation, deurbanization, and
       <a href="/wiki/Barbarian" title="Barbarian">
        barbarian
       </a>
       invasion, all of which had begun in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">
        Late Antiquity
       </a>
       . The barbarian invaders formed their own new kingdoms in the remains of the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">
        Western Roman Empire
       </a>
       . In the 7th century, North Africa and the Middle East, once part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" title="Eastern Roman Empire">
        Eastern Roman Empire
       </a>
       , became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">
        Caliphate
       </a>
       after conquest by
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
        Muhammad
       </a>
       's successors. Although there were substantial changes in society and political structures, the break was not as extreme as once put forth by historians, with most of the new kingdoms incorporating as many of the existing Roman institutions as they could. Christianity expanded in western Europe, and monasteries were founded. In the 7th and 8th centuries the
       <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">
        Franks
       </a>
       , under the
       <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_dynasty" title="Carolingian dynasty">
        Carolingian dynasty
       </a>
       , established an empire covering much of western Europe;
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       it lasted until the 9th century, when it succumbed to pressure from new invaders—the
       <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">
        Vikings
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarians#Entering_the_Carpathian_Basin_(c._895)" title="Hungarians">
        Magyars
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Saracen" title="Saracen">
        Saracens
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Notre_Dame_de_ParisA02-04.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="504" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Notre_Dame_de_ParisA02-04.jpg/100px-Notre_Dame_de_ParisA02-04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Notre_Dame_de_ParisA02-04.jpg/150px-Notre_Dame_de_ParisA02-04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Notre_Dame_de_ParisA02-04.jpg/200px-Notre_Dame_de_ParisA02-04.jpg 2x" width="100"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Notre_Dame_de_ParisA02-04.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Cathedral" title="Notre Dame Cathedral">
          Notre Dame Cathedral
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
          Paris
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
          France
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">
        High Middle Ages
       </a>
       , which began after 1000, the population of Europe increased greatly as technological and agricultural innovations allowed trade to flourish and crop yields to increase.
       <a href="/wiki/Manorialism" title="Manorialism">
        Manorialism
       </a>
       —the organization of peasants into villages that owed rents and labour service to nobles—and
       <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">
        feudalism
       </a>
       —a political structure whereby
       <a href="/wiki/Knight" title="Knight">
        knights
       </a>
       and lower-status nobles owed military service to their overlords in return for the right to rents from lands and
       <a href="/wiki/Manor" title="Manor">
        manors
       </a>
       —were two of the ways of organizing medieval society that developed during the High Middle Ages. Kingdoms became more centralized after the decentralizing effects of the breakup of the
       <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">
        Carolingian Empire
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">
        Crusades
       </a>
       , first preached in 1095, were an attempt by western Christians from countries such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">
        Kingdom of England
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">
        Kingdom of France
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
        Holy Roman Empire
       </a>
       to regain control of the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">
        Holy Land
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
        Muslims
       </a>
       and succeeded long enough to establish some Christian states in the Near East. Also, merchants imported thousands of
       <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">
        Armenians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">
        Circassians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">
        Georgians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">
        Greeks
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">
        Slavs
       </a>
       into
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       to work as household slaves and in processing
       <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">
        sugar
       </a>
       . Intellectual life was marked by
       <a href="/wiki/Scholasticism" title="Scholasticism">
        scholasticism
       </a>
       and the founding of universities, while the building of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gothic_cathedrals" title="Gothic cathedrals">
        Gothic cathedrals
       </a>
       was one of the outstanding artistic achievements of the age.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">
        Late Middle Ages
       </a>
       were marked by difficulties and calamities. Famine, plague and war devastated the population of western Europe.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">
        Black Death
       </a>
       alone killed approximately 75 to 200 million people between 1347 and 1350.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was one of the deadliest pandemics in human history. Starting in Asia, the disease reached Mediterranean and western
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       during the late 1340s,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and killed tens of millions of Europeans in six years; between a third and a half of the population perished.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Middle Ages witnessed the first sustained
       <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">
        urbanization
       </a>
       of northern and western Europe. Many modern European states owe their origins to events unfolding in the Middle Ages; present European political boundaries are, in many regards, the result of military and dynastic events during this tumultuous period.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Middle Ages lasted until the beginning of the
       <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">
        Early modern period
       </a>
       in the 16th century,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       marked by the rise of
       <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">
        nation states
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001280_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001280-97">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the division of Western
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">
        Reformation
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill1999319–23_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill1999319–23-98">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the rise of
       <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">
        humanism
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">
        Italian Renaissance
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill1999267–68_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill1999267–68-99">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the beginnings of European overseas expansion which allowed for the
       <a href="/wiki/Columbian_Exchange" title="Columbian Exchange">
        Columbian Exchange
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sub-Saharan_Africa">
        Sub-Saharan Africa
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Africa" title="History of Africa">
        History of Africa
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WLA_metmuseum_Head_of_an_Oba_16th_century.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/WLA_metmuseum_Head_of_an_Oba_16th_century.jpg/100px-WLA_metmuseum_Head_of_an_Oba_16th_century.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/WLA_metmuseum_Head_of_an_Oba_16th_century.jpg/150px-WLA_metmuseum_Head_of_an_Oba_16th_century.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/WLA_metmuseum_Head_of_an_Oba_16th_century.jpg/200px-WLA_metmuseum_Head_of_an_Oba_16th_century.jpg 2x" width="100"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WLA_metmuseum_Head_of_an_Oba_16th_century.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Brass" title="Brass">
          Brass
         </a>
         "
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benin_bronze" title="Benin bronze">
          Benin bronze
         </a>
         ",
         <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
          Nigeria
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Medieval
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">
        Sub-Saharan Africa
       </a>
       was home to many different civilizations. The
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">
        Kingdom of Aksum
       </a>
       declined in the 7th century as Islam cut it off from its Christian allies and its people moved further into the
       <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Highlands" title="Ethiopian Highlands">
        Ethiopian Highlands
       </a>
       for protection. They eventually gave way to the
       <a href="/wiki/Zagwe_dynasty" title="Zagwe dynasty">
        Zagwe dynasty
       </a>
       who are famed for their rock cut architecture at
       <a href="/wiki/Lalibela" title="Lalibela">
        Lalibela
       </a>
       . The Zagwe would then fall to the
       <a href="/wiki/Solomonic_dynasty" title="Solomonic dynasty">
        Solomonic dynasty
       </a>
       who claimed descent from the Aksumite emperors
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and would rule the country well into the 20th century. In the West African
       <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">
        Sahel
       </a>
       region, many Islamic empires rose, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">
        Ghana Empire
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">
        Mali Empire
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">
        Songhai Empire
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kanem_Empire" title="Kanem Empire">
        Kanem Empire
       </a>
       . They controlled the
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">
        trans-Saharan trade
       </a>
       in gold, ivory, salt and slaves.
      </p>
      <p>
       South of the Sahel, civilizations rose in the coastal forests where horses and camels could not survive.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       These include the
       <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">
        Yoruba
       </a>
       city of
       <a href="/wiki/Ife" title="Ife">
        Ife
       </a>
       , noted for its art,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Oyo_Empire" title="Oyo Empire">
        Oyo Empire
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Benin_Empire" title="Benin Empire">
        Benin Empire
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Edo_people" title="Edo people">
        Edo people
       </a>
       centred in
       <a href="/wiki/Benin_City" title="Benin City">
        Benin City
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">
        Igbo
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nri" title="Kingdom of Nri">
        Kingdom of Nri
       </a>
       which produced advanced bronze art at
       <a href="/wiki/Igbo-Ukwu" title="Igbo-Ukwu">
        Igbo-Ukwu
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">
        Akan
       </a>
       who are noted for their intricate architecture.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Central Africa saw the birth of several states, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">
        Kingdom of Kongo
       </a>
       . In what is now modern
       <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">
        Zimbabwe
       </a>
       various kingdoms such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mutapa" title="Kingdom of Mutapa">
        Kingdom of Mutapa
       </a>
       descended from the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mapungubwe" title="Kingdom of Mapungubwe">
        Kingdom of Mapungubwe
       </a>
       in modern
       <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">
        South Africa
       </a>
       . They flourished through trade with the
       <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">
        Swahili people
       </a>
       on the East African coast. They built large defensive stone structures without mortar such as
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Zimbabwe" title="Great Zimbabwe">
        Great Zimbabwe
       </a>
       , capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Zimbabwe" title="Kingdom of Zimbabwe">
        Kingdom of Zimbabwe
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Khami" title="Khami">
        Khami
       </a>
       , capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Butua" title="Kingdom of Butua">
        Kingdom of Butua
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Danangombe" title="Danangombe">
        Danangombe
       </a>
       (Dhlo-Dhlo), capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Rozwi_Empire" title="Rozwi Empire">
        Rozwi Empire
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">
        Swahili people
       </a>
       themselves were the inhabitants of the East African coast from Kenya to Mozambique who traded extensively with Asians and Arabs, who introduced them to Islam. They built many port cities such as
       <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">
        Mombasa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">
        Zanzibar
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kilwa_Kisiwani" title="Kilwa Kisiwani">
        Kilwa
       </a>
       , which were known to Chinese sailors under
       <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">
        Zheng He
       </a>
       and Islamic geographers.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="South_Asia">
        South Asia
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">
        History of India
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hoysala_emblem.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1776" data-file-width="1184" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hoysala_emblem.JPG/100px-Hoysala_emblem.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hoysala_emblem.JPG/150px-Hoysala_emblem.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hoysala_emblem.JPG/200px-Hoysala_emblem.JPG 2x" width="100"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hoysala_emblem.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chennakesava_Temple" title="Chennakesava Temple">
          Chennakesava Temple
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belur" title="Belur">
          Belur
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
          India
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In northern
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">
        India
       </a>
       , after the fall (550 CE) of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">
        Gupta Empire
       </a>
       , the region divided into a complex and fluid network of smaller kingly states.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Early Muslim incursions began in the west in 712 CE, when the Arab
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
        Umayyad Caliphate
       </a>
       annexed much of present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">
        Pakistan
       </a>
       . Arab military advance was largely halted at that point, but Islam still spread in India, largely due to the influence of Arab merchants along the western coast. The
       <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Struggle" title="Tripartite Struggle">
        Tripartite Struggle
       </a>
       for control of northern India took place in the ninth century. The struggle was between the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pratihara_Empire" title="Pratihara Empire">
        Pratihara Empire
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">
        Pala Empire
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rashtrakuta_Empire" title="Rashtrakuta Empire">
        Rashtrakuta Empire
       </a>
       . Some of the important states that emerged in India at this time included the
       <a href="/wiki/Bahmani_Sultanate" title="Bahmani Sultanate">
        Bahmani Sultanate
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">
        Vijayanagara Empire
       </a>
       . Post-classical dynasties in South India included those of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty" title="Chalukya dynasty">
        Chalukyas
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Rashtrakuta_dynasty" title="Rashtrakuta dynasty">
        Rashtrakutas
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hoysala_dynasty" title="Hoysala dynasty">
        Hoysalas
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">
        Cholas
       </a>
       , the Islamic
       <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">
        Mughals
       </a>
       , the Marathas and the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mysore" title="Kingdom of Mysore">
        Mysores
       </a>
       . Science, engineering, art, literature, astronomy, and philosophy flourished under the patronage of these kings.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="East_Asia">
        East Asia
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_East_Asia" title="History of East Asia">
        History of East Asia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       After a period of relative disunity, the
       <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">
        Sui dynasty
       </a>
       reunified China in 581,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and under the succeeding
       <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">
        Tang dynasty
       </a>
       (618–907) China entered a
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age" title="Golden Age">
        Golden Age
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis20091_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis20091-101">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Tang dynasty eventually splintered, however, and after
       <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period">
        half a century of turmoil
       </a>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Song_Dynasty" title="Northern Song Dynasty">
        Song Dynasty
       </a>
       reunified China,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       when it was, according to
       <a href="/wiki/William_H._McNeill_(historian)" title="William H. McNeill (historian)">
        William McNeill
       </a>
       , the "richest, most skilled, and most populous country on earth".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill198250_102-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill198250-102">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Pressure from nomadic empires to the north became increasingly urgent. By 1142, North China had been lost to the
       <a href="/wiki/Jurchen_people" title="Jurchen people">
        Jurchens
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Jin%E2%80%93Song_Wars" title="Jin–Song Wars">
        Jin–Song Wars
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">
        Mongol Empire
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_China" title="Mongol invasion of China">
        conquered all of China
       </a>
       in 1279, along with almost half of Eurasia's landmass. After about a century of Mongol
       <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">
        Yuan dynasty
       </a>
       rule, the ethnic Chinese reasserted control with the founding of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">
        Ming dynasty
       </a>
       (1368).
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1462" data-file-width="4334" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg/300px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg/450px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg/600px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Battle during
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Japan" title="Mongol invasion of Japan">
          1281 Mongol invasion of Japan
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Japan" title="History of Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       , the imperial lineage had been established by this time, and during the
       <a href="/wiki/Asuka_period" title="Asuka period">
        Asuka period
       </a>
       (538–710) the
       <a href="/wiki/Yamato_Province" title="Yamato Province">
        Yamato Province
       </a>
       developed into a clearly centralized state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HOJ_104-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HOJ-104">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       was introduced, and there was an emphasis on the adoption of elements of Chinese culture and
       <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">
        Confucianism
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Nara_period" title="Nara period">
        Nara period
       </a>
       of the 8th century
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       marked the emergence of a strong Japanese state and is often portrayed as a golden age.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       During this period, the imperial government undertook great public works, including government offices, temples, roads, and irrigation systems.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Heian_period" title="Heian period">
        Heian period
       </a>
       (794 to 1185) saw the peak of imperial power, followed by the rise of militarized clans, and the beginning of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_Japan" title="Medieval Japan">
        Japanese feudalism
       </a>
       . The feudal period of Japanese history, dominated by powerful regional lords (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Daimy%C5%8D" title="Daimyō">
         daimyōs
        </a>
       </i>
       ) and the military rule of warlords (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dgun" title="Shōgun">
         shōguns
        </a>
       </i>
       ) such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Ashikaga_shogunate" title="Ashikaga shogunate">
        Ashikaga shogunate
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">
        Tokugawa shogunate
       </a>
       , stretched from 1185 to 1868. The emperor remained, but mostly as a figurehead, and the power of merchants was weak.
      </p>
      <p>
       Postclassical
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Korea" title="History of Korea">
        Korea
       </a>
       saw the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms_of_Korea" title="Three Kingdoms of Korea">
        Three Kingdoms
       </a>
       era, the three kingdoms being
       <a href="/wiki/Goguryeo" title="Goguryeo">
        Goguryeo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Baekje" title="Baekje">
        Baekje
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Silla" title="Silla">
        Silla
       </a>
       . Silla conquered Baekje in 660, and Goguryeo in 668,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       marking the beginning of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/North%E2%80%93South_States_Period" title="North–South States Period">
         North–South States Period
        </a>
       </i>
       (남북국시대), with
       <a href="/wiki/Later_Silla" title="Later Silla">
        Unified Silla
       </a>
       in the south and
       <a href="/wiki/Balhae" title="Balhae">
        Balhae
       </a>
       , a successor state to Goguryeo, in the north.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 892 CE, this arrangement reverted to the
       <a href="/wiki/Later_Three_Kingdoms" title="Later Three Kingdoms">
        Later Three Kingdoms
       </a>
       , with Goguryeo (then called
       <a href="/wiki/Taebong" title="Taebong">
        Taebong
       </a>
       and eventually named
       <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">
        Goryeo
       </a>
       ) emerging as dominant, unifying the entire peninsula by 936.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kta_p113_108-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kta_p113-108">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The founding Goryeo dynasty ruled until 1392, succeeded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">
        Joseon
       </a>
       , which ruled for approximately 500 years.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia">
        Southeast Asia
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angkor_wat_temple.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="448" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Angkor_wat_temple.jpg/220px-Angkor_wat_temple.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Angkor_wat_temple.jpg/330px-Angkor_wat_temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Angkor_wat_temple.jpg/440px-Angkor_wat_temple.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angkor_wat_temple.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">
          Angkor Wat
         </a>
         temple,
         <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">
          Cambodia
         </a>
         , early 12th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Southeast_Asia" title="History of Southeast Asia">
        History of Southeast Asia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The beginning of the Middle Ages in Southeast Asia saw the fall (550 CE) of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Funan_(Southeast_Asia)" title="Funan (Southeast Asia)">
        Kingdom of Funan
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Chenla" title="Chenla">
        Chenla Empire
       </a>
       , which was then replaced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">
        Khmer Empire
       </a>
       (802 CE). The Khmer's capital city
       <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">
        Angkor
       </a>
       was the largest city in the world prior to the industrial age and contained over a thousand temples, the most famous being
       <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">
        Angkor Wat
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhothai_Kingdom" title="Sukhothai Kingdom">
        Sukhothai
       </a>
       (1238 CE) and
       <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">
        Ayutthaya
       </a>
       (1351 CE) kingdoms were major powers of the
       <a href="/wiki/Thai_people" title="Thai people">
        Thai people
       </a>
       , who were influenced by the Khmer. Starting in the 9th century, the
       <a href="/wiki/Pagan_Kingdom" title="Pagan Kingdom">
        Pagan Kingdom
       </a>
       rose to prominence in modern
       <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">
        Myanmar
       </a>
       . Other notable kingdoms of the period include the
       <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">
        Srivijayan Empire
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Lavo_Kingdom" title="Lavo Kingdom">
        Lavo Kingdom
       </a>
       (both coming into prominence in the 7th century), the
       <a href="/wiki/Champa" title="Champa">
        Champa
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Hariphunchai" title="Hariphunchai">
        Hariphunchai
       </a>
       (both about 750), the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dai_Viet" title="Dai Viet">
        Dai Viet
       </a>
       (968),
       <a href="/wiki/Lan_Na" title="Lan Na">
        Lan Na
       </a>
       (13th century),
       <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">
        Majapahit
       </a>
       (1293),
       <a href="/wiki/Lan_Xang" title="Lan Xang">
        Lan Xang
       </a>
       (1354), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ava" title="Kingdom of Ava">
        Kingdom of Ava
       </a>
       (1364).
       <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_aborigines" title="Taiwanese aborigines">
        Taiwanese aborigines
       </a>
       formed tribal alliances such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Middag" title="Kingdom of Middag">
        Kingdom of Middag
       </a>
       . It was also during this period that Islam spread to present-day Indonesia (beginning in the 13th century), and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malay_states" title="Malay states">
        Malay states
       </a>
       began to emerge including the
       <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Sultanate" title="Malacca Sultanate">
        Malacca Sultanate
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Empire" title="Bruneian Empire">
        Bruneian Empire
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Rajahnate_of_Maynila" title="Rajahnate of Maynila">
        Rajahnate of Maynila
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">
        Oceania
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ahu_Tongariki,_15_moais.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2896" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG/220px-Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG/330px-Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG/440px-Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ahu_Tongariki,_15_moais.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Moai" title="Moai">
          Moai
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui" title="Rapa Nui">
          Rapa Nui
         </a>
         (Easter Island)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Oceania" title="History of Oceania">
        History of Oceania
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Tu%CA%BBi_Tonga_Empire" title="Tuʻi Tonga Empire">
        Tuʻi Tonga Empire
       </a>
       was founded in the 10th century CE and expanded between 1200 and 1500. Tongan culture, language, and hegemony spread widely throughout Eastern Melanesia, Micronesia and Central Polynesia during this period,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       influencing East 'Uvea, Rotuma, Futuna, Samoa and Niue, as well as specific islands / parts of Micronesia (Kiribati, Pohnpei, the
       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">
        Mariana Islands
       </a>
       populated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_people" title="Chamorro people">
        Chamorro people
       </a>
       and miscellaneous outliers), Vanuatu, and New Caledonia (specifically, the
       <a href="/wiki/Loyalty_Islands" title="Loyalty Islands">
        Loyalty Islands
       </a>
       , with the main island being predominantly populated by the Melanesian
       <a href="/wiki/Kanak_people" title="Kanak people">
        Kanak people
       </a>
       and their cultures).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At around the same time, a powerful
       <a href="/wiki/Thalassocracy" title="Thalassocracy">
        thalassocracy
       </a>
       appeared in Eastern Polynesia centred around the
       <a href="/wiki/Society_Islands" title="Society Islands">
        Society Islands
       </a>
       , specifically on the sacred
       <a href="/wiki/Taputapuatea_marae" title="Taputapuatea marae">
        Taputapuatea marae
       </a>
       , which drew in Eastern Polynesian colonists from places as far away as Hawai'i, New Zealand (
       <a href="/wiki/Aotearoa" title="Aotearoa">
        Aotearoa
       </a>
       ), and the Tuamotu Islands for political, spiritual and economic reasons, until the unexplained collapse of regular long-distance voyaging in the Eastern Pacific a few centuries before Europeans began exploring the area. Indigenous written records from this period are virtually non-existent, as it seems that all Pacific Islanders, with the possible exception of the enigmatic
       <a href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui_people" title="Rapa Nui people">
        Rapa Nui
       </a>
       and their currently undecipherable
       <a href="/wiki/Rongorongo" title="Rongorongo">
        Rongorongo
       </a>
       script, had no writing systems of any kind until after their introduction by European colonists; however, some indigenous prehistories can be estimated and academically reconstructed through careful, judicious analysis of native oral traditions, colonial ethnography, archaeology, physical anthropology and linguistics research.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Americas">
        The Americas
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Machu_Picchu,_Per%C3%BA,_2015-07-30,_DD_47.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5763" data-file-width="8669" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG/220px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG/330px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG/440px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Machu_Picchu,_Per%C3%BA,_2015-07-30,_DD_47.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Machu_Picchu" title="Machu Picchu">
          Machu Picchu
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">
          Inca Empire
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
          Peru
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Americas" title="History of the Americas">
        History of the Americas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Central_America" title="History of Central America">
        History of Central America
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_America" title="History of South America">
        History of South America
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_America" title="History of North America">
        History of North America
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In North America, this period saw the rise of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">
        Mississippian culture
       </a>
       in the modern
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       c. 800 CE, marked by the extensive 12th-century urban complex at
       <a href="/wiki/Cahokia" title="Cahokia">
        Cahokia
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Ancestral_Puebloans" title="Ancestral Puebloans">
        Ancestral Puebloans
       </a>
       and their predecessors (9th – 13th centuries) built extensive permanent settlements, including stone structures that would remain the largest buildings in North America until the 19th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFagan200535_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFagan200535-111">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">
        Mesoamerica
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">
        Teotihuacan
       </a>
       civilization fell and the
       <a href="/wiki/Classic_Maya_collapse" title="Classic Maya collapse">
        Classic Maya collapse
       </a>
       occurred. The
       <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">
        Aztec Empire
       </a>
       came to dominate much of
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">
        Mesoamerica
       </a>
       in the 14th and 15th centuries. In
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       , the 14th and 15th centuries saw the rise of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inca" title="Inca">
        Inca
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">
        Inca Empire
       </a>
       of Tawantinsuyu, with its capital at
       <a href="/wiki/Cusco" title="Cusco">
        Cusco
       </a>
       , spanned the entire Andes Mountain Range, making it the most extensive Pre-Columbian civilization. The Inca were prosperous and advanced, known for an excellent
       <a href="/wiki/Inca_road_system" title="Inca road system">
        road system
       </a>
       and unrivaled
       <a href="/wiki/Masonry" title="Masonry">
        masonry
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">
        Modern history
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">
        Modern history
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">
        Modern history
       </a>
       (the "modern period," the "modern era," "modern times") is history of the period following the Middle Ages. "
       <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_history" title="Contemporary history">
        Contemporary history
       </a>
       " is history that only covers events from around 1945 to the present day.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">
        Early modern period
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
