       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">
        Early modern period
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       "
       <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">
        Early modern period
       </a>
       "
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [b]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a term used by historians to refer to the period between the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Post-classical_history" title="Post-classical history">
        Post-classical history
       </a>
       ) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
        Industrial Revolution
       </a>
       —roughly 1500 to 1800.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595_13-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Early Modern period is characterized by the rise of science, and by increasingly rapid
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_technology" title="History of technology">
        technological progress
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">
        secularized
       </a>
       civic
       <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">
        politics
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">
        nation state
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capitalist_economy" title="Capitalist economy">
        Capitalist economies
       </a>
       began their rise, initially in northern
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republics
       </a>
       such as
       <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">
        Genoa
       </a>
       . The Early Modern period also saw the rise and dominance of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">
        mercantilist
       </a>
       economic theory. As such, the Early Modern period represents the decline and eventual disappearance, in much of the European sphere, of
       <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">
        feudalism
       </a>
       , serfdom and the power of the
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Catholic Church
       </a>
       . The period includes the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">
        Protestant Reformation
       </a>
       , the disastrous
       <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">
        Thirty Years' War
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">
        Age of Discovery
       </a>
       , European
       <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">
        colonial expansion
       </a>
       , the peak of European
       <a href="/wiki/Witch-hunt" title="Witch-hunt">
        witch-hunting
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_revolution" title="Scientific revolution">
        Scientific revolution
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">
        Age of Enlightenment
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [c]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance">
        Renaissance
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3070" data-file-width="2258" height="299" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour.jpg/220px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour.jpg/330px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour.jpg/440px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">
          da Vinci
         </a>
         's
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Vitruvian_Man" title="Vitruvian Man">
           Vitruvian Man
          </a>
         </i>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">
          Renaissance
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
          Italy
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">
        Renaissance
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">
        Renaissance
       </a>
       , beginning in the 14th century and extending into the 16th, consisted of the rediscovery of the
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">
        classical
       </a>
       world's scientific contributions, and of the
       <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">
        economic
       </a>
       and social rise of Europe. The Renaissance also engendered a culture of
       <a href="/wiki/Curiosity" title="Curiosity">
        inquisitiveness
       </a>
       which ultimately led to
       <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">
        Humanism
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis2012250–53_114-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis2012250–53-114">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">
        Scientific Revolution
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013683–85_115-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013683–85-115">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although it saw social and political upheaval and revolutions in many
       <a href="/wiki/Intellectual" title="Intellectual">
        intellectual
       </a>
       pursuits, the Renaissance is perhaps known best for its
       <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">
        artistic
       </a>
       developments
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and the contributions of such
       <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">
        polymaths
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">
        Leonardo da Vinci
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">
        Michelangelo
       </a>
       , who inspired the term "
       <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">
        Renaissance man
       </a>
       ."
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_expansion">
        European expansion
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Europe" title="History of Europe">
        History of Europe
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">
        Age of Discovery
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">
        Colonialism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/16th_century" title="16th century">
        16th century
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/17th_century" title="17th century">
        17th century
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:187px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3942" data-file-width="5788" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg/185px-OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg/278px-OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg/370px-OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg 2x" width="185"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Ortelius#Map_publisher" title="Abraham Ortelius">
          1570 world map
         </a>
         , with Europeans' discoveries
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During this period, European powers came to dominate most of the world. Although the most developed regions of European classical civilization were more urbanized than any other region of the world, European civilization had undergone a lengthy period of gradual decline and collapse. During the Early Modern Period, Europe was able to regain its dominance; historians still debate the causes.
      </p>
      <p>
       Europe's success in this period stands in contrast to other regions. For example, one of the most advanced civilizations of the Middle Ages was China. It had developed an advanced
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monetary_economy" title="Monetary economy">
        monetary economy
       </a>
       by 1,000 CE. China had a free
       <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">
        peasantry
       </a>
       who were no longer subsistence farmers, and could sell their produce and actively participate in the market. According to
       <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">
        Adam Smith
       </a>
       , writing in the 18th century, China had long been one of the richest, most fertile, best cultivated, most industrious, most urbanized, and most prosperous countries in the world. It enjoyed a technological advantage and had a monopoly in
       <a href="/wiki/Cast_iron" title="Cast iron">
        cast iron
       </a>
       production, piston bellows,
       <a href="/wiki/Suspension_bridge" title="Suspension bridge">
        suspension bridge
       </a>
       construction,
       <a href="/wiki/Printing" title="Printing">
        printing
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Compass" title="Compass">
        compass
       </a>
       . However, it seemed to have long since stopped progressing.
       <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">
        Marco Polo
       </a>
       , who visited China in the 13th century, describes its cultivation, industry, and populousness almost in the same terms as travelers would in the 18th century.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gutenburg_bible.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="460" data-file-width="386" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Gutenburg_bible.jpg/220px-Gutenburg_bible.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Gutenburg_bible.jpg/330px-Gutenburg_bible.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Gutenburg_bible.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gutenburg_bible.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Gutenberg_Bible" title="Gutenberg Bible">
          Gutenberg Bible
         </a>
         , produced using
         <a href="/wiki/Movable_type" title="Movable type">
          movable type
         </a>
         c. 1450
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       One theory of Europe's rise holds that Europe's
       <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">
        geography
       </a>
       played an important role in its success. The Middle East, India and China are all ringed by mountains and oceans but, once past these outer barriers, are nearly flat. By contrast, the
       <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">
        Pyrenees
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">
        Alps
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Apennine_Mountains" title="Apennine Mountains">
        Apennines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">
        Carpathians
       </a>
       and other mountain ranges run through Europe, and the continent is also divided by several seas. This gave Europe some degree of protection from the peril of Central Asian invaders. Before the era of firearms, these nomads were militarily superior to the agricultural states on the periphery of the Eurasian continent and, as they broke out into the plains of northern India or the valleys of China, were all but unstoppable. These invasions were often devastating. The
       <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">
        Golden Age of Islam
       </a>
       was ended by the
       <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">
        Mongol
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258)" title="Siege of Baghdad (1258)">
        sack of Baghdad
       </a>
       in 1258. India and China were subject to periodic
       <a href="/wiki/Invasion" title="Invasion">
        invasions
       </a>
       , and Russia spent a couple of centuries under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tatar_invasions" title="Tatar invasions">
        Mongol-Tatar
       </a>
       yoke. Central and western Europe, logistically more distant from the Central Asian heartland, proved less vulnerable to these threats.
      </p>
      <p>
       Geography contributed to important
       <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">
        geopolitical
       </a>
       differences. For most of their histories, China, India, and the Middle East were each unified under a single dominant power that expanded until it reached the surrounding mountains and deserts.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In 1600 the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       controlled almost all the Middle East,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEImber200266_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEImber200266-116">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">
        Ming dynasty
       </a>
       ruled China,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEbreyWalthallPalais2006_117-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEbreyWalthallPalais2006-117">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001376–77_118-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001376–77-118">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">
        Mughal Empire
       </a>
       held sway over India. By contrast, Europe was almost always divided into a number of warring states. Pan-European empires, with the notable exception of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , tended to collapse soon after they arose. Another doubtless important geographic factor in the rise of Europe was the Mediterranean Sea, which, for millennia, had functioned as a maritime superhighway fostering the exchange of goods, people, ideas and inventions.
      </p>
      <p>
       Nearly all the agricultural civilizations have been heavily constrained by their
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">
        environments
       </a>
       . Productivity remained low, and
       <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">
        climatic
       </a>
       changes easily instigated
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boom-and-bust" title="Boom-and-bust">
        boom-and-bust
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Business_cycle" title="Business cycle">
        cycles
       </a>
       that brought about civilizations' rise and fall. By about 1500, however, there was a qualitative change in world history.
       <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">
        Technological
       </a>
       advance and the
       <a href="/wiki/Wealth" title="Wealth">
        wealth
       </a>
       generated by
       <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">
        trade
       </a>
       gradually brought about a widening of possibilities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Many have also argued that Europe's institutions allowed it to expand, that
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Property_right" title="Property right">
        property rights
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">
        free-market
       </a>
       economics were stronger than elsewhere due to an ideal of
       <a href="/wiki/Political_freedom" title="Political freedom">
        freedom
       </a>
       peculiar to Europe. In recent years, however, scholars such as
       <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Pomeranz" title="Kenneth Pomeranz">
        Kenneth Pomeranz
       </a>
       have challenged this view. Europe's maritime expansion unsurprisingly—given the continent's geography—was largely the work of its Atlantic states: Portugal, Spain, England, France, and the Netherlands. Initially the
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empires
       </a>
       were the predominant conquerors and sources of influence, and their union resulted in the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">
        Iberian Union
       </a>
       , the first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_empire" title="Global empire">
        global empire
       </a>
       on which the "
       <a href="/wiki/The_empire_on_which_the_sun_never_sets" title="The empire on which the sun never sets">
        sun never set
       </a>
       ". Soon the more northern English, French and Dutch began to dominate the Atlantic. In a series of wars fought in the 17th and 18th centuries, culminating with the
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </a>
       , Britain emerged as the new world power.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_developments">
        Regional developments
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_(Holy_Wisdom)_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1130" data-file-width="1700" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_(Holy_Wisdom)_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">
          Hagia Sophia
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">
          Istanbul
         </a>
         (formerly
         <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">
          Constantinople
         </a>
         ),
         <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
          Turkey
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">
        Persia
       </a>
       came under the rule of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safavid_Empire" title="Safavid Empire">
        Safavid Empire
       </a>
       in 1501, succeeded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty" title="Afsharid dynasty">
        Afsharid Empire
       </a>
       in 1736, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">
        Qajar Empire
       </a>
       in 1796. Areas to the north and east were held by
       <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">
        Uzbeks
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pashtuns" title="Pashtuns">
        Pashtuns
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       , after taking
       <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">
        Constantinople
       </a>
       in 1453, quickly gained control of the Middle East, the
       <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">
        Balkans
       </a>
       , and most of North Africa.
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Africa" title="History of Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       , this period saw a decline in many civilizations and an advancement in others. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swahili_Coast" title="Swahili Coast">
        Swahili Coast
       </a>
       declined after coming under Portuguese (and later
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Oman" title="History of Oman">
        Omani
       </a>
       ) control. In west Africa, the
       <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">
        Songhai Empire
       </a>
       fell to the Moroccans in 1591 when they invaded with guns. The South African
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Zimbabwe" title="Kingdom of Zimbabwe">
        Kingdom of Zimbabwe
       </a>
       gave way to smaller kingdoms such as
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mutapa" title="Kingdom of Mutapa">
        Mutapa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Butua" title="Kingdom of Butua">
        Butua
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Rozwi_Empire" title="Rozwi Empire">
        Rozwi
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
        Ethiopia
       </a>
       suffered from the 1531 invasion from neighbouring Muslim
       <a href="/wiki/Adal_Sultanate" title="Adal Sultanate">
        Adal Sultanate
       </a>
       , and in 1769 entered the
       <a href="/wiki/Zemene_Mesafint" title="Zemene Mesafint">
        Zemene Mesafint
       </a>
       (Age of Princes) during which the Emperor became a figurehead and the country was ruled by warlords, though the royal line later would recover under Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Tewodros_II" title="Tewodros II">
        Tewodros II
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Ajuran_Sultanate" title="Ajuran Sultanate">
        Ajuran Empire
       </a>
       , in the
       <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">
        Horn of Africa
       </a>
       , began to decline in the 17th century, succeeded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_the_Geledi" title="Sultanate of the Geledi">
        Geledi Sultanate
       </a>
       . Other civilizations in Africa advanced during this period. The
       <a href="/wiki/Oyo_Empire" title="Oyo Empire">
        Oyo Empire
       </a>
       experienced its golden age, as did the
       <a href="/wiki/Benin_Empire" title="Benin Empire">
        Benin Empire
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire" title="Ashanti Empire">
        Ashanti Empire
       </a>
       rose to power in what is modern day
       <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">
        Ghana
       </a>
       in 1670. The
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">
        Kingdom of Kongo
       </a>
       also thrived during this period. European
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Africa" title="Exploration of Africa">
        exploration of Africa
       </a>
       reached its zenith at this time.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG/220px-Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG/330px-Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG/440px-Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" title="Ming Dynasty">
          Ming Dynasty
         </a>
         section,
         <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">
          Great Wall of China
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the Far East, the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_China" title="History of China">
        Chinese
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" title="Ming Dynasty">
        Ming Dynasty
       </a>
       gave way (1644) to the
       <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">
        Qing
       </a>
       , the last Chinese imperial dynasty, which would rule until 1912.
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Japan" title="History of Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       experienced its
       <a href="/wiki/Azuchi%E2%80%93Momoyama_period" title="Azuchi–Momoyama period">
        Azuchi–Momoyama period
       </a>
       (1568–1603), followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">
        Edo period
       </a>
       (1603–1868). The
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Korea" title="History of Korea">
        Korean
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseon_Dynasty" title="Joseon Dynasty">
        Joseon Dynasty
       </a>
       (1392–1910) ruled throughout this period, successfully repelling 16th- and 17th-century invasions from Japan and China. Japan and China were significantly affected during this period by expanded maritime trade with Europe, particularly the Portuguese in Japan. During the Edo period, Japan would pursue isolationist policies, to eliminate foreign influences.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1681" data-file-width="2040" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/220px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/330px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/440px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Taj_Mahal" title="Taj Mahal">
          Taj Mahal
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">
          Mughal Empire
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
          India
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On the
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">
        Indian subcontinent
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">
        Delhi Sultanate
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Deccan_sultanates" title="Deccan sultanates">
        Deccan sultanates
       </a>
       would give way, beginning in the 16th century, to the
       <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">
        Mughal Empire
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Starting in the northwest, the Mughal Empire would by the late 17th century come to rule the entire subcontinent,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       except for the southernmost Indian provinces, which would remain independent. Against the Muslim Mughal Empire, the Hindu
       <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Empire" title="Maratha Empire">
        Maratha Empire
       </a>
       was founded on the west coast in 1674, gradually gaining territory—a majority of present-day India—from the Mughals over several decades, particularly in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mughal%E2%80%93Maratha_Wars" title="Mughal–Maratha Wars">
        Mughal–Maratha Wars
       </a>
       (1681–1701). The Maratha Empire would in 1818 fall under the control of the British
       <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">
        East India Company
       </a>
       , with all former Maratha and Mughal authority devolving in 1858 to the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">
        British Raj
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1511 the Portuguese overthrew the
       <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Sultanate" title="Malacca Sultanate">
        Malacca Sultanate
       </a>
       in present-day Malaysia and Indonesian
       <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">
        Sumatra
       </a>
       . The Portuguese held this important trading territory (and the valuable associated navigational strait) until overthrown by the Dutch in 1641. The
       <a href="/wiki/Johor_Sultanate" title="Johor Sultanate">
        Johor Sultanate
       </a>
       , centred on the southern tip of the Malay Peninsula, became the dominant trading power in the region.
       <a href="/wiki/Western_imperialism_in_Asia" title="Western imperialism in Asia">
        European colonization
       </a>
       expanded with the Dutch in the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">
        Netherlands East Indies
       </a>
       , and the Spanish in the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines" title="History of the Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       . Into the 19th century, European expansion would affect the whole of Southeast Asia, with the British in
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Myanmar" title="History of Myanmar">
        Myanmar
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Malaysia" title="History of Malaysia">
        Malaysia
       </a>
       , and the establishment of
       <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">
        French Indochina
       </a>
       . Only
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Thailand" title="History of Thailand">
        Thailand
       </a>
       would successfully resist colonization.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Pacific islands of
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Oceania" title="History of Oceania">
        Oceania
       </a>
       would also be affected by European contact, starting with the circumnavigational voyage of
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">
        Ferdinand Magellan
       </a>
       , who landed on the
       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">
        Marianas
       </a>
       and other islands in 1521. Also notable were the voyages (1642–44) of
       <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">
        Abel Tasman
       </a>
       to present-day Australia, New Zealand and nearby islands, and the voyages (1768–1779) of Captain
       <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">
        James Cook
       </a>
       , who made the first recorded European contact with
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Hawaii" title="History of Hawaii">
        Hawaii
       </a>
       . Britain would found its first colony on Australia in 1788.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_chapel_at_Fort_Ross_(2016).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3559" data-file-width="5339" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Russian_chapel_at_Fort_Ross_%282016%29.jpg/220px-Russian_chapel_at_Fort_Ross_%282016%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Russian_chapel_at_Fort_Ross_%282016%29.jpg/330px-Russian_chapel_at_Fort_Ross_%282016%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Russian_chapel_at_Fort_Ross_%282016%29.jpg/440px-Russian_chapel_at_Fort_Ross_%282016%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_chapel_at_Fort_Ross_(2016).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Russian chapel,
         <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ross,_California" title="Fort Ross, California">
          Fort Ross, California
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US" title="US">
          US
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Americas" title="History of the Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">
        western European powers
       </a>
       vigorously colonized the newly discovered continents, largely displacing the
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
        indigenous populations
       </a>
       , and destroying the advanced civilizations of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">
        Aztecs
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inca" title="Inca">
        Inca
       </a>
       . Spain, Portugal, Britain, and France all made extensive territorial claims, and undertook large-scale settlement, including the importation of large numbers of African
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Americas" title="Slavery in the Americas">
        slaves
       </a>
       . Portugal claimed
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brazil" title="History of Brazil">
        Brazil
       </a>
       . Spain claimed the rest of
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_America" title="History of South America">
        South America
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">
        Mesoamerica
       </a>
       , and southern
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_America" title="History of North America">
        North America
       </a>
       . Britain colonized the east coast of North America, and France colonized the central region of North America. Russia made incursions onto the northwest coast of North America, with a first colony in present-day
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Alaska" title="History of Alaska">
        Alaska
       </a>
       in 1784, and the outpost of
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ross,_California" title="Fort Ross, California">
        Fort Ross
       </a>
       in present-day
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_California" title="History of California">
        California
       </a>
       in 1812.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1762, in the midst of the
       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">
        Seven Years' War
       </a>
       , France secretly ceded most of its North American claims to Spain in the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fontainebleau_(1762)" title="Treaty of Fontainebleau (1762)">
        Treaty of Fontainebleau
       </a>
       . Thirteen of the British colonies declared independence as the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States" title="History of the United States">
        United States of America
       </a>
       in 1776, ratified by the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">
        Treaty of Paris
       </a>
       in 1783, ending the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">
        American Revolutionary War
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">
        Napoleon Bonaparte
       </a>
       won France’s claims back from Spain in the
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </a>
       in 1800, but sold them to the United States in 1803 as the
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">
        Louisiana Purchase
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russia" title="History of Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ivan_the_Terrible" title="Ivan the Terrible">
        Ivan the Terrible
       </a>
       was crowned (1547) the first
       <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">
        Tsar
       </a>
       of Russia, and by annexing the Turkic Khanates in the east, transformed Russia into a regional power. The countries of western Europe, while expanding prodigiously through technological advancement and colonial conquest, competed with each other economically and militarily in a state of almost constant
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_1500%E2%80%931799" title="List of wars 1500–1799">
        war
       </a>
       . Often the wars had a
       <a href="/wiki/European_wars_of_religion" title="European wars of religion">
        religious dimension
       </a>
       , either Catholic versus Protestant, or (primarily in eastern Europe) Christian versus Muslim. Wars of particular note include the
       <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">
        Thirty Years' War
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">
        War of the Spanish Succession
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">
        Seven Years' War
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">
        French Revolutionary Wars
       </a>
       . Napoleon came to power in France in 1799, an event foreshadowing the Napoleonic Wars of the early 19th century.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Late_Modern_period">
        Late Modern period
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span id="1750.E2.80.931914">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1750–1914">
        1750–1914
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/18th_century" title="18th century">
        18th century
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/19th_century" title="19th century">
        19th century
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Long_nineteenth_century" title="Long nineteenth century">
        Long nineteenth century
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_Imperialism" title="Age of Imperialism">
        Age of Imperialism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Revolution" title="Age of Revolution">
        Age of Revolution
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_Revolution" title="Diplomatic Revolution">
        Diplomatic Revolution
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
        Industrial Revolution
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="1024" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/220px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/330px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/440px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/James_Watt" title="James Watt">
          Watt
         </a>
         's
         <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">
          steam engine
         </a>
         powered the
         <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
          Industrial Revolution
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">
        Scientific Revolution
       </a>
       changed humanity's understanding of the world and led to the
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
        Industrial Revolution
       </a>
       , a major transformation of the world's economies. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">
        Scientific Revolution
       </a>
       in the 17th century had had little immediate effect on industrial
       <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">
        technology
       </a>
       ; only in the second half of the 18th century did scientific advances begin to be applied substantially to practical
       <a href="/wiki/Invention" title="Invention">
        invention
       </a>
       . The Industrial Revolution began in
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">
        Great Britain
       </a>
       and used new modes of production—the
       <a href="/wiki/Factory" title="Factory">
        factory
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">
        mass production
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mechanization" title="Mechanization">
        mechanization
       </a>
       —to manufacture a wide array of goods faster and using less labour than previously required. The Age of Enlightenment also led to the beginnings of modern
       <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">
        democracy
       </a>
       in the late-18th century
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">
        American
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">
        French Revolutions
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">
        Democracy
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">
        republicanism
       </a>
       would grow to have a profound effect on world events and on
       <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">
        quality of life
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="1560" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/260px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/390px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/520px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png 2x" width="260"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">
          Empires
         </a>
         , 1898
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After Europeans had achieved influence and control over the Americas,
       <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">
        imperial
       </a>
       activities turned to the lands of Asia and Oceania. In the 19th century the European states had social and technological advantage over Eastern lands.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Britain gained control of the Indian subcontinent, Egypt and the
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia" title="Peninsular Malaysia">
        Malay Peninsula
       </a>
       ; the
       <a href="/wiki/Cochinchina_Campaign" title="Cochinchina Campaign">
        French took Indochina
       </a>
       ; while the Dutch cemented their control over the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">
        Dutch East Indies
       </a>
       . The British also colonized Australia, New Zealand and South Africa with large numbers of British colonists emigrating to these colonies. Russia colonized large pre-agricultural areas of Siberia. In the late 19th century, the European powers
       <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">
        divided the remaining areas of Africa
       </a>
       . Within Europe, economic and military challenges created a system of
       <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">
        nation states
       </a>
       , and ethno-linguistic groupings began to identify themselves as distinctive nations with aspirations for cultural and political autonomy. This
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">
        nationalism
       </a>
       would become important to peoples across the world in the 20th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Industrial_Revolution" title="Second Industrial Revolution">
        Second Industrial Revolution
       </a>
       , the world economy became reliant on
       <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">
        coal
       </a>
       as a fuel, as new methods of
       <a href="/wiki/Transport" title="Transport">
        transport
       </a>
       , such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railways" title="Railways">
        railways
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Steamship" title="Steamship">
        steamships
       </a>
       , effectively shrank the world. Meanwhile, industrial
       <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">
        pollution
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">
        environmental
       </a>
       damage, present since the discovery of fire and the beginning of civilization, accelerated drastically.
      </p>
      <p>
       The advantages that Europe had developed by the mid-18th century were two: an
       <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">
        entrepreneurial
       </a>
       culture,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the wealth generated by the Atlantic trade (including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_slave_trade" title="African slave trade">
        African slave trade
       </a>
       ). By the late 16th century,
       <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">
        silver
       </a>
       from the Americas accounted for the Spanish empire's wealth.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The profits of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">
        slave trade
       </a>
       and of
       <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">
        West Indian
       </a>
       plantations amounted to 5% of the
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Economic history of the United Kingdom">
        British economy
       </a>
       at the time of the
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
        Industrial Revolution
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While some historians conclude that, in 1750,
       <a href="/wiki/Workforce_productivity" title="Workforce productivity">
        labour productivity
       </a>
       in the most developed regions of China was still on a par with that of Europe's Atlantic economy,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       other historians like
       <a href="/wiki/Angus_Maddison" title="Angus Maddison">
        Angus Maddison
       </a>
       hold that the per-capita productivity of western Europe had by the late
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       surpassed that of all other regions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="1914.E2.80.931945">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1914–1945">
        1914–1945
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">
        20th century
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">
        Interwar period
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">
        Roaring Twenties
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
        Great Depression
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="672" data-file-width="950" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg/220px-Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg/330px-Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg/440px-Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
          World War I
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Trench_warfare" title="Trench warfare">
          trench warfare
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nagasakibomb.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3877" data-file-width="3245" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/220px-Nagasakibomb.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/330px-Nagasakibomb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/440px-Nagasakibomb.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nagasakibomb.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings" title="Atomic bombings">
          Atomic bombings
         </a>
         :
         <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">
          Hiroshima
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">
          Nagasaki
         </a>
         , 1945
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The 20th century opened with Europe at an apex of wealth and power, and with much of the world under its direct
       <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">
        colonial
       </a>
       control or its indirect domination. Much of the rest of the world was influenced by heavily Europeanized nations: the United States and Japan. As the century unfolded, however, the global system dominated by rival powers was subjected to severe strains, and ultimately seemed to yield to a more fluid structure of independent nations organized on Western models.
      </p>
      <p>
       This transformation was
       <a href="/wiki/Catalysis" title="Catalysis">
        catalysed
       </a>
       by wars of unparalleled scope and devastation.
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       destroyed many of Europe's empires and monarchies, and weakened Britain and France. In its aftermath, powerful ideologies arose. The
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">
        Russian Revolution
       </a>
       of 1917 created the first
       <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">
        communist
       </a>
       state, while the 1920s and 1930s saw
       <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">
        militaristic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">
        fascist
       </a>
       dictatorships gain control in Italy, Germany, Spain and elsewhere.
      </p>
      <p>
       Ongoing national rivalries, exacerbated by the economic turmoil of the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
        Great Depression
       </a>
       , helped precipitate
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">
        militaristic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">
        dictatorships
       </a>
       of Europe and Japan pursued an ultimately doomed course of
       <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">
        imperialist
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">
        expansionism
       </a>
       . Their defeat opened the way for the advance of communism into Central Europe, Yugoslavia, Bulgaria, Romania, Albania, China, North Vietnam, and North Korea.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_history">
        Contemporary history
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_history" title="Contemporary history">
        Contemporary history
       </a>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span id="1945.E2.80.932000">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1945–2000">
        1945–2000
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">
        20th century
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
        Cold War
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">
        Green Revolution
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">
        Space exploration
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Digital_Revolution" title="Digital Revolution">
        Digital Revolution
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1434" data-file-width="1024" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg/220px-My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg/330px-My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg/440px-My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Civilians (here,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/My_Lai" title="My Lai">
          My Lai
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viet_Nam" title="Viet Nam">
          Viet Nam
         </a>
         , 1968) suffered greatly in 20th-century wars.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       When
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       ended in 1945, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       was founded in the hope of preventing future wars,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fasulo1_126-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fasulo1-126">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as the
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       had been formed following
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The war had left two countries, the United States and the Soviet Union, with principal power to influence international affairs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Each was suspicious of the other and feared a global spread of the other's, respectively
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capitalist" title="Capitalist">
        capitalist
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist">
        communist
       </a>
       , political-economic model. This led to the
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
        Cold War
       </a>
       , a forty-five-year stand-off and
       <a href="/wiki/Arms_race" title="Arms race">
        arms race
       </a>
       between the United States and its allies, on one hand, and the Soviet Union and its allies on the other. With the development of
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">
        nuclear weapons
       </a>
       during World War II, and with their subsequent proliferation, all of humanity were put at risk of
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_warfare" title="Nuclear warfare">
        nuclear war
       </a>
       between the two superpowers, as demonstrated by
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_nuclear_close_calls" title="List of nuclear close calls">
        many incidents
       </a>
       , most prominently the October 1962
       <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">
        Cuban Missile Crisis
       </a>
       . Such war
       <a href="/wiki/Global_catastrophic_risk#Warfare_and_mass_destruction" title="Global catastrophic risk">
        being viewed as impractical
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">
        proxy wars
       </a>
       were instead waged, at the expense of non-nuclear-armed
       <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">
        Third World
       </a>
       countries.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Cold War ended in 1991, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union disintegrated
       </a>
       , in part due to inability to compete economically with the United States and western Europe. However, the United States likewise began to show signs of slippage in her geopolitical influence;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1995155_129-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1995155-129">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       even as her
       <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">
        private sector
       </a>
       , now less inhibited by the claims of the
       <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">
        public sector
       </a>
       , increasingly sought private advantage to the prejudice of the public
       <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">
        weal
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2018)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the early postwar decades, the African and Asian colonies of the Belgian, British, Dutch, French, and other west European empires won their formal independence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbernethy2000133_130-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbernethy2000133-130">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       But the newly independent countries faced challenges in the form of
       <a href="/wiki/Neocolonialism" title="Neocolonialism">
        neocolonialism
       </a>
       , sociopolitical disarray, poverty, illiteracy, and
       <a href="/wiki/Endemic_(epidemiology)" title="Endemic (epidemiology)">
        endemic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_disease" title="Tropical disease">
        tropical diseases
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Most Western European and Central European countries gradually formed a political and economic community, the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       , which expanded eastward to include former
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_satellites" title="Soviet satellites">
        Soviet-satellite countries
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The European Union's effectiveness was handicapped by the immaturity of its common economic and political institutions, somewhat comparable to the inadequacy of United States institutions under the
       <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">
        Articles of Confederation
       </a>
       prior to the adoption of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Constitution" title="U.S. Constitution">
        U.S. Constitution
       </a>
       that came into force in 1789. Asian and African countries followed suit and began taking tentative steps toward forming their own respective continental associations.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4029" data-file-width="3904" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg/220px-Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg/330px-Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg/440px-Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Last Moon landing:
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">
          Apollo 17
         </a>
         (1972)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Cold War preparations to deter or to fight a third world war accelerated advances in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technologies" title="Technologies">
        technologies
       </a>
       that, though conceptualized before World War II, had been implemented for that war's exigencies, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">
        jet aircraft
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">
        rocketry
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_computers" title="Electronic computers">
        electronic computers
       </a>
       . In the decades after World War II, these advances led to jet travel,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artificial_satellite" title="Artificial satellite">
        artificial satellites
       </a>
       with innumerable applications including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_positioning_system" title="Global positioning system">
        global positioning systems
       </a>
       (GPS), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">
        Internet
       </a>
       —inventions that have revolutionized the movement of people, ideas, and information.
      </p>
      <p>
       However, not all scientific and technological advances in the second half of the 20th century required an initial military impetus. That period also saw ground-breaking developments such as the discovery of the structure of
       <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">
        DNA
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
        <a href="#cite_note-135">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the consequent sequencing of the
       <a href="/wiki/Human_genome" title="Human genome">
        human genome
       </a>
       , the worldwide
       <a href="/wiki/Smallpox#Eradication" title="Smallpox">
        eradication of smallpox
       </a>
       , the discovery of
       <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">
        plate tectonics
       </a>
       , manned and unmanned
       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">
        exploration of space
       </a>
       and of previously inaccessible parts of mankind's
       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
        home planet
       </a>
       , and foundational discoveries in
       <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">
        physics
       </a>
       phenomena ranging from the smallest entities (
       <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">
        particle physics
       </a>
       ) to the greatest entity (
       <a href="/wiki/Physical_cosmology" title="Physical cosmology">
        physical cosmology
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       The century saw several
       <a href="/wiki/Global_catastrophic_risk" title="Global catastrophic risk">
        global threats
       </a>
       emerge or become more serious or more widely recognized, including
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation" title="Nuclear proliferation">
        nuclear proliferation
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_climate_change" title="Global climate change">
        global climate change
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
        deforestation
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">
        ocean acidification
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">
        overpopulation
       </a>
       , deadly
       <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">
        epidemics
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbe" title="Microbe">
        microbial
       </a>
       diseases,
       <a href="/wiki/Near-Earth_object" title="Near-Earth object">
        near-Earth asteroids and comets
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BROWN02_139-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BROWN02-139">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Supervolcano" title="Supervolcano">
        supervolcano
       </a>
       eruptions,
       <a href="/wiki/Gamma-ray_burst#Hypothetical_effects_on_Earth_in_the_past" title="Gamma-ray burst">
        lethal gamma-ray bursts
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Geomagnetic_storm" title="Geomagnetic storm">
        geomagnetic storms
       </a>
       destroying all electronic equipment, and the dwindling of global
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">
        natural resources
       </a>
       (particularly
       <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">
        fossil fuels
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">
        21st century
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="785" data-file-width="590" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg/220px-Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg/330px-Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg/440px-Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">
          Ballistic missile
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">
        21st century
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       A man-made hazard to world survival that dominated concerns in the second half of the 20th century, continues into the 21st. Countries ambitious to develop and deploy
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" title="Nuclear weapons">
        nuclear weapons
       </a>
       are discouraged from doing so by countries that already possess them. At the same time, nuclear-armed countries have shown little urgency about honoring their
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons">
        20th-century pledge to eventually eliminate all nuclear weapons
       </a>
       . Such weapons continue to be equally hazardous to their owners as to their potential targets.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Internet_map_1024.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1280" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Internet_map_1024.jpg/220px-Internet_map_1024.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Internet_map_1024.jpg/330px-Internet_map_1024.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Internet_map_1024.jpg/440px-Internet_map_1024.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Internet_map_1024.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Partial map of
         <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">
          Internet
         </a>
         , 2005
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The 21st century has been marked by growing
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_globalization" title="Economic globalization">
        economic globalization
       </a>
       and integration, with consequent increased risk to interlinked economies; and by the expansion of communications with
       <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">
        mobile phones
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">
        Internet
       </a>
       , which have caused fundamental
       <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">
        societal
       </a>
       changes in business, politics, and individuals' personal lives.
      </p>
      <p>
       The early 21st century saw escalating intra- and international strife in the Near East and Afghanistan, stimulated by vast economic disparities, by dissatisfaction with governments dominated by Western interests, by inter-ethnic and inter-sectarian feuds, and by the longest war in the history of the United States, the proximate cause for which was
       <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">
        Osama bin Laden
       </a>
       's provocative
       <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
        2001 destruction
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="World Trade Center (1973–2001)">
        World Trade Center
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       US military involvements in the Near East and Afghanistan drained US economic resources at a time when the US and other Western countries were experiencing mounting socioeconomic dislocations aggravated by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robotization" title="Robotization">
        robotization
       </a>
       of work and the
       <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_country_sourcing" title="Low-cost country sourcing">
        exportation of industries to cheaper-workforce countries
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:12-05-08_AS1.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/220px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/330px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/440px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
